Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And the ancients called it "contused cure," and it is that you should shave the hair from the forehead of the patient who has this illness, then make three incisions on the forehead equally along the length of the forehead; and let one of the incisions be like two fingers in the middle of the forehead extending downwards to the nose, and the other two at the two sides above the eyelids, and guard against cutting the arteries that are on the two sides above the eyelids; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jawbones, and let each wound be the size of three joined fingers across; and have prepared a piece of sponge and many cloths to wipe the blood, then place the sharp spatula on both sides of which this is the form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision that is near the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the skin that is between the two incisions to the whole surface that is on the bone, then do likewise from the middle incision to the other second, and then remove this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	then place in the first incision the instrument that is called "cultellary," and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side it is smooth, not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge towards the flesh next to the skin, and the smooth edge towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the middle incision.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous to that which appears of the skin, and then likewise do in the middle incision to the other outside; and then draw out the blood equally, and press the place for the blood taken; then put in each incision a tent of old cotton, and put on cloths moistened in wine and oil and vinegar, and guard against hot abscesses coming there; and on the third day untie the bandage, and administer a great abundance of warm water, then treat it with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and with other treatments with which wounds are treated, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the rheum of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone has an acute catarrh habitually, and you see the eyes watery and small, and weakened vision, and the eyelids burned; and the hair falls out, and there is severe headache, and the patient sneezes; then know by these symptoms that those matters and that catarrh do not come forth except from many veins, and the best treatment that there is, is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you instruct the patient to raise his forehead, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another at the temple.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the incision of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move in chewing; and when the bone is uncovered, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then separate between the two lips of the incision and put in old cotton, and linen tents; then bind above cloths moistened in wine and oil, and guard against a hot abscess; when it is removed, it is necessary that you rub the bone until flesh begins to grow there, then treat it with drying things, which cause flesh to grow.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour, and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster; and apply it to these wounds to make flesh grow everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping up of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of four things: either grains, or an animal, or a mine stone or something similar such as iron; or seeds, such as millet, beans, peas; or flowing things such as water and vinegar and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or other thing falls into the ear that does not adhere to the ear, nor grow in the ear, put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then instill some drops of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and make him sneeze with sneezing powder, and plug his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and extend the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often it comes out by this cure; and if it does not come out, administer extraction with fine forceps, of which here is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it leaps out with forceps, that is good; if not, administer extraction with a fine probe of small diameter; and if it does not come out by this, make a chain of bronze and put the head of the chain into the opening of the ear strongly, and plug that which is around the chain with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the chain; then pull it out forcefully, for very often it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, take birdlime, and put on it some instrument that is pointed to do this, and put a little cotton around it; then press the birdlime onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out by all these things that we have said, hasten to cut open the ear before a hot abscess and spasm come; and the manner of the incision is that you first bleed the patient from the cephalic vein, and extract blood according to the measure of his strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn his ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear, at the fat or the dependent place; and let the incision be like a crescent moon, until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck it quickly into your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is inside and it swells, administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer a thin spatula according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think that the grain is moist because of the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with fine forceps and by sucking, as we have said, so that the extraction is easy.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	If water falls into the ear, the patient should first use sneezing powder and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him lie on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it leaps out because of this, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, take many stones, according to the length of your little finger, and light ones, and warm them a little in the fire; and let the patient put one into the opening of his ear, and stand on his feet on the other side, and strike with another stone on the stone which is in the ear; and do not cease doing this stone by stone until all the water comes out, and thus it all leaps out; and if you wish, take a reed, and put one end in the ear, and take the other end and set it on fire until the most of the reed is burnt; then do the same with other reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said with the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is small, like a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is large enough that one can feel it, administer extraction with tweezers; and this is the easiest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms engendered in the ears, when you cure it as we have said in the division and in the treatise on distillations, and the cure does not help, then you must look at the ear in the sun: if any worms appear, draw them out with fine tweezers, and if they do not appear, take the cane of which this is the form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And put the thinnest end into the ear according to the amount the patient can tolerate, then suck strongly on the whole cane; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey in coming out, then plug around the cane with cotton as I have said in the case of the stone; and if they do not jump out as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven in killing worms, and you will find them in the treatise on distillations; and distill your oils and your medicines into the ear with this instrument, of which this is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be of silver or bronze, narrow below with a small hole, and open above for distilling; and to press the distillation inside, use a well-made bronze instrument for this, and if you wish take a razor and wrap cotton neatly around the point; then pour your oil or your juice, and whatever you wish of your medicines into the cane, and the cane should be in the ear; then put the razor with the cotton inside, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled to the end of the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and let the distillation be slightly warmed by fire before it is distilled into the ear; and be careful that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping up of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	Some children are born without any opening in their ears; and this same thing happens to adults through the blocking of a wound, or of flesh growing inside the ear, and this blockage sometimes happens deep in the ear, so that one cannot see it; and sometimes a little of the opening remains, and one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which happens deep inside, so that one cannot see it, is difficult to cure in many cases, and in that which one sees it is necessary that you put the patient's ear in the sun; and look inside: if you see the obstruction clearly, then work with this spatula of which this is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting in front and behind, completely flat, so that it does not injure the ear; if the obstruction is of flesh grown or body of the ear, then hold it with fine pincers, and cut it lightly, until that flesh is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the obstruction is deep in the ear, then take a thin, light scraper and heat it a little in the fire, then put it into the ear canal.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the obstruction from which the patient feels pain in hearing, pierce it lightly, and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a tent according to the width of the opening, and moisten it in Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for a few days until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and moisten it in rosewater, and sprinkle on powdered vitriol; and if you see the ear swollen, then you must remove the tent and use another tent moistened in cerate made from rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then treat it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, soak a sponge and cloth in cold water, and apply it to the ear, and use other treatments that stop bleeding which are in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of the eyelids
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	These small boils that come on the eyelids when they are moist and dry, you must stretch them with tongs and pincers, and cut them with a spatula from their roots; then put on the area powdered vitriol.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if pus flows out, cauterize it with a fine lenticular cautery, and cauterization after incision is useful; and often they return, when something remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the hail (or, of the frost/hoar frost)
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Often, things appear on the eyelids that resemble hail in form and hardness, and for this reason this illness is called "hail," and it is a gathering of thick moisture on the eyelid above and below; the procedure is as follows: observe if the hail moves from one side to another, and this is easy to know; then cut it lengthwise, then lightly scrape each part, then grasp it with pincers, and cut it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cut it without piercing the eyelid a little, it does not harm the patient; and if the cut is large, close it with a suture, and treat it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not use force, for ointments restore it quickly and generate flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hail descends into the inside of the ear towards the upper part, invert the eyelid, and grasp the hail with pincers, and cut and press it from one side to the other; and if the eyelid is separated by the incision, it does not harm; and when the hail is cut, wash the eye with salt water, and treat the area with something that generates flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	Of the eyelid fat (or, of the fat of the eyelids)
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is generated in the tissues of the upper eyelids, and this happens more to children than to anyone else, and it greatly harms their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and they cannot look at the sunlight because tears flow from their eyes; and therefore they always lie on their faces, and sleep on them, and their eyelids below their eyebrows are moist where the swelling and appearance have covered the exinach which appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the area with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient puts his head in your lap; and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains the exinach from each part, then put it on him; and press with your fingers on one side and the other, so that the exinach is gathered in the middle of the circle; then cut in the middle of the moisture with a sharp spatula a slit of the width, and let it not be larger than the incision that one makes to bleed a vein; and cut the skin completely until you reach the exinach; and in several cases the exinach comes from the incision, according to the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then extract it all in one piece with a piece of lint between your fingers from the outside, and turn your hand to the right and to the left until it is separated; and be careful not to insert the spatula into the incision, that you do not come with the whole spatula right up to the eye, lest you injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exinach does not appear at the beginning of the incision, slightly enlarge the incision a little until it appears; then extract it as we have said, then moisten cloths in wine and water, and apply them to the area, and bind it with a bandage.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are some men who grind salt and apply it to corrupt the remaining moisture.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess appears in the place, treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the testicles
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow on the testicles that are not natural, and are thick, they harm the eyes and cause various diseases such as habitual tears and softening of the testicles and albuginea, so much so that it causes their destruction; and the treatment is according to four methods: either by cautery with fire, or by a sharp medicine as it is described in the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and suture or by cautery, as I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the patient's head on your lap, then turn the eyelid with your left hand; if it is turned, it is good; if not, put a needle with a thread on it; and let this be near the edge of the eyelid where the hairs grow near those hairs, and pull the thread above with the eyelid, and turn it toward the forehead; then cut in the part under the eyelid, under the extra hairs, with a sharp spatula, from the larger tear duct to the smaller; then pull out the thread, and place under the eyelid a small tent of cotton and cloth, then mark on the eyelid the shape of a wedge, like a myrtle leaf, and however it is necessary that the shape should be according to the amount you want to raise the eyelid which is divided in two.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is someone who needs a large amount of the eyelid to be cut according to how much the eyelid is softened; then cut with the spatula along the two lines that you have marked, and begin from the larger tear duct to the smaller; and let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the oncin in one of the two corners of the heart, then scrape it all; then join the two lips with a suture of a needle with a thin woolen thread, and wipe away the blood, and stick the surplus of the threads above the two eyebrows with some sticky substance, if you want to do this; and if not, do not worry about it, then leave the suture and the threads for three or four days; then treat the wound without suturing with drying and constricting substances, for the eyelid rises at the healing of the wound and its joining, but the suture is better (as the ancients said), and this is a work without fear; and there is another method: and it is that you mark the eyelid with a shape that is like a myrtle leaf, as we have described, with three incisions separated according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what is above with small, equal forces according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you are not able to hold the forceps, and the thing is not even, then take a needle with a thread, and put it in the middle of the shape; and put another thread near the larger tear duct, and the second thread near the smaller, and bring the threads together evenly between your fingers; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin on which you have marked, as we have described, then join the two lips of the wound by suture, and treat it until it is healed; and if an abscess forms at your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyelid are inverted: then you must use what we have said about the incision; but the suture in one and the other is more skillful.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of canulas is according to this form: and it is that you turn the eyelid and cut into it as I have said, and then make two canulas by art, and two thin threads as long as the eyelid and as wide as the spatula is; and cut at the two ends of the two parts where you hold the threads; then join the one and the other subtly on what overhangs from the eyelid, and pull the two canulas firmly from the two parts; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin that is pulled will die and wither and rot, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, then cut it with some force, then treat it until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, and the eyelid is raised, and the hairs will no longer prick; and this is the form of the two canulas that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The procedure is such that you take a fine needle, and put in it a soft and fine silk thread; then join the ends and knot one and the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then arrange in the sheath another fine silk thread briefly, and knot the ends of the thread; then let the patient put his head in your lap; and let it be near the sun so that the operation is clear, for this is a subtle and delicate operation, then put the needle with the whole sheath into the root of the ingrown hair, and make it pierce into the eyelid quickly until you draw it out above the natural hair; then pull the hair up to the sheath, and put in the sheath that hair, if there is one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand until the hairs come out with the whole sheath into the eyelid with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the sheath is pulled and the hairs do not come out with it, then you will pull the sheath underneath with all the thread that you have arranged in it, until the sheath comes out from the hole above and you see it by the vision of the eye; then you will pull the sheath and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair settles in its place and the flesh grows over it; and if the hair is small, then attach a long hair from the natural eyelashes, and let it be raised with that or leave it, until it is lengthened and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the corruption of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or corruption comes to the eye, there are two kinds: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or a cut, or a cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of working on it is that you split that suture, and separate the lips of it, and put linen tents inside, and bind it until it is healed; and it is not necessary that you use in the cure of it things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do that, the disease returns worse than before; but work with softening things, such as fenugreek; and rose water or mallow and linseed cooked, and diachylon ointment melted in some oil, and wrap a tent, and cure it with that.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not heal according to the form that it was before; and this work that we have spoken of is nothing but a dressing for this disease, that it may not return according to the form that it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that grows in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is below, which truly is called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidental comes from a wound and a fissure and a cautery and similar things; and the way of working on it is that you take a needle, in which there is a double thread, and stick it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear duct to the right, so that the thread comes out at two ends of the flesh; then stretch the flesh above with the needle, and cut it a span wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the eyelid returns as it should, it is good; if not, take a razor and place it in the fissure, and turn the eyelid, and make two incisions on the inside of the eyelid; and let the ends of the two incisions be at the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and make an angle so that when they are joined, the shape is like the shape of a letter which is called "I griesche"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its sides are sharp underneath, of that which follows the eyelid, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a woolen thread; then cure it with what we have said of emollient medicines, and of tents, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a fissure or a suture or a cautery, then you must make a full incision under the hairs of the eyelids, and according to what is above; then separate between the two lips with a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise master prepares tools to the best of his ability to restore the shape to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what is needed in work and instruments in several ways.
dou soudement de la papiere	From the sudden swelling of the eyelid.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this adhesion happens to many men in such a way that the upper eyelid is adhered to the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must put the point of a razor under the eyelid, and lift it up; and stretch it with forceps, until you cut what is attached with a thin spatula, which is not too sharp or too cutting, so that the patient cannot suffer that the too sharp spatula wounds the eye; and let your incision, with which you peel off that adhesion, be slight, so that the eyelid returns to its natural form; and this adhesion is healed, and sometimes they use salted water in the eye, and rinse it with fresh water, and with egg white; then place between the eyelid and the eye a linen tent, and put on the eye wool soaked in egg white; and after the third day, use egg white and soothing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the corner of the eye.
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the growth in the corner of the eye is of two kinds: one is sinewy and similar to a hard membrane, and another which is not sinewy, but is similar to congealed white moisture, so that when one touches it with iron and tries to grasp it with forceps, one cannot; and both types begin near the lacrimal gland, and grow little by little until they cover the whole vision and all the light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is that the patient puts his head in your lap, then opens his eyes; and lift the eyelid with your hand, then grasp the growth with small double forceps, and stretch it upwards; then take a needle, and thread it with a horsehair, or cowhair, or oxhair, and a strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little and stick it into the growth, and pierce it with the whole needle, and tie the growth with a thread and stretch it upwards, and peel off with the hair the side of the growth which follows the pupil and the silk with the hair down to the head, then cut the remaining part at the root of the tear duct with the thin spatula and the small forceps, and leave the natural flesh at the tear duct, so that the flow of tears is not impeded by the incision; and sometimes the growth is only stretched with the hook and with the thread, as we have said; then it is peeled off with the smooth spatula of which here is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And take care that the spatula does not touch the fleshy membrane and break it, and that the pupil is not pierced; and after the incision, put a little crushed salt and egg white made with litharge into the eye, and leave it until the next day; then treat it with what is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the growth is not sinewy, and you cannot insert the needle, and the hook cannot enter it, many times this kind of growth is cured with medicines; and they arise as I have recounted in the division, and if you wish to cut it, then open the eye of the patient, and take the light spatula slightly sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And scrape the growth from above subtly, and if you see that it diminishes little by little and the scraping hastens it, then distil from your mouth into the eye egg white made with litharge and red egg white and crushed salt, and plug the eye until the next day; then recommence the other operation according to this same procedure, until it is entirely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If anything is obstructing the eye, such as a hot abscess, then leave it, and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then recommence the operation as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the tear duct harms the eye by great annoyance, then lift it with a hook, and cut part of it and not all, so that the tear duct is not injured; then instill into the eye red egg white which is made with litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In the eyes of some men, a red flesh sometimes grows, and covers the pupil and extends over the eyelids and turns them outward, and resembles a pomegranate blossom; and the operation is that the patient places his head in your lap, then you open his eyes, and lift all that flesh with hooks suitable for this, and hold it firmly; then cut the first flesh, and continue cutting with a razor to the end, and be careful that you do not injure the eye during the operation; and let the incision be with the spatula that we have described in the incision of the growth and with small instruments with which one removes the sebaceous material, as the figure after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is completed and all the flesh removed, fill the eye with crushed salt or instill red egg white and similar corrosive medicines, and place on the outside of the eye cotton with egg white, so that it is protected from a hot abscess; and if anything remains, and the hot blood overwhelms you, and you fear a hot abscess, then leave the eye and treat the abscess with things that soothe a hot abscess; then return to your operation until it is healed, and do so as long as flesh is added to the eye in this way.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, it is necessary that you ease the treatment of each weak eye by natural means; and by accidental means, with iron instruments; and do not put your hand to any of these operations until you see that the limb can tolerate that operation.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Sebaceous material are red veins that are found on the eye, and they hinder vision and weaken the eye daily.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary, first, that you observe if the eye, in which the sebaceous material is, is healthy, and there is no other disease except the sebaceous material; then lift it in this manner: instruct the patient to place his head in your lap, then lift those veins with a hook according to your judgment, and let the hooks be doubled, thin, according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two hooks, graded, in one body, according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then lift those veins skillfully, and blood will flow, one drop after another, until you see those veins removed from the eye; and be careful not to injure the eye with the tips of the spatulas, and do this work at midday before the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you cut only those veins; and when you have done this, instill green and red vitriol into the eye to corrode what remains of the sebaceous material.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are not able to remove all of it at that time, apply a plaster to the eye of things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is eased and the danger of a hot abscess is past, then begin again in the same manner as before until it is healed; and this is the shape of the hooks:
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The physicians call this fistula "arissati": when you treat it with cautery and with burning medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, the method is to incise the abscess, where it should mature, and drain all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, scrape it with the instrument whose shape is shown here; and it is called "aspre chief", and is made of tempered iron with a round head, and is pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the spot of the corrupt bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is removed; and do this several times, then restore the place with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the place is healed, and flesh grows there, and the body of the fistula is healed, and remains so for forty days, and it does not renew itself and is not abscessed, and no bad accident occurs, know that it is healed; if not, there is no other method than to return the fistula to the opening of the nose according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with burning medicines, and when it is uncovered take a drill according to this form, and let the head of iron be three-angled, and the shaft be thinned to the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone near the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then turn the drill completely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it because the wind comes out if he holds his hand over his nose; and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and the place hardens, the matter goes to the nose; it is an easier thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the discharge of the eye.
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is completely open, and there is no obstruction or narrowing of the nose, you must bind the patient; then cleanse it, then apply cupping glasses or scarification without wounding to draw out the humor, then apply to the eye a poultice made of acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla, then bind the eye, and apply the poultice with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take fairly soft cloths, and fold each into four, and then place one on top of the other according to the amount the eye needs; then bind it tightly on top with a firm bandage, and repeat the cupping glasses to draw out the humor without wounding; then remove the cupping glasses and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the poultice softens, you must bind it very tightly; then remove the poultice after a day and night, and if you see the eye recovering, that is good; if not, then repeat the poultice and cloths and the binding and the cupping glasses until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Of the rupture of the uvea.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a rupture occurs in the uvea, then it opens, and there comes forth matter like grains of resin, and it is frightening to see; then if you see it torn, the procedure is such that you insert a needle into the root of the lower part up to the upper part, then insert another needle where there is a double thread from the part of the tear duct; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to its position; then cut the place of the double thread and tie a part of the uvea around, and bind it well, then remove the needle and apply to the eye wool moistened in egg white; and leave it until the thread falls off with the uvea, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the uvea on each side with a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye shows great swelling, pierce it with a fine spatula that reaches deep into the eye, and let the albuminous humor flow out and the eye subside, and it will enter immediately; then remove it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	Of the bow of the eye.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This illness which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but a bow which is gathered in the eye, resembling descending water, and it is not water; and the manner of the appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands on two sides, and move it until you see the bow come to the top to your eyes; then let it be pierced, and let it descend and the light be cleared, and let the patient see things as he was used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the bow is not as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then make the patient sit between your hands, then take the fine spatula and pierce the cornea slightly through the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the iris, until the bow comes out; and when it has come out, distill into the eye warm water mixed with honey, or water in which fenugreek has been boiled and honey, then let it be treated with other treatments until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	Of the waters of the eye.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have already the similarities of the waters in the division, and what is necessary for piercing; so work according to the health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light because of the sun, and bind the healthy eye and squeeze it very tightly; then put the eyelid on your left hand if the eye is left, or on your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument which is called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then put the point of the instrument next to the iris by the thickness of a ray in that whiteness of the eye at the part of the smaller tear duct, then push the instrument which is called "almagda" skillfully, and turn your hand until it pierces the whiteness of the eye, and feel that the almagda reaches the empty space; and it is necessary that the measure of the almagda's path be to the depth of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the blackness; and this is the iris of the eye; then you will see the bone in that eyelid because of the clarity of the cornea, and then put the instrument to the place where the water is, then press it out one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water descends immediately, the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	Afterwards rest a little, and if the water rises the second way, push with the instrument, and when it is firmly fixed and does not rise, withdraw the almagda lightly by turning your hand little by little; and then put a little rock salt in the water, and lift the eye with this.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put over the eye tampons or wool soaked in rose oil and egg white, and bind it with the healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, put on crushed cumin with egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are such men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument which is called "alberit", of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce then only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make a subtle opening, then put in the almagda, as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a suitable bed, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and let him be free from all movement, and let him take light foods, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and let him be bandaged according to his disposition until the next day; then unbind him in that same dark room, and test his vision, and make him see some things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this at the time of the cure or immediately after the incision, but you must delay this, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If a warm abscess comes, that you unbind the eye before the seventh day, and treat it with something that soothes the abscess; and when it is calmed, then unbind the vision and put on its face a small pillow to cover it for a few days, and let it always be in that dark room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then he should leave the house little by little, and return to his usual activities; and know that no apprentice should meddle in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And a man came to us who was from Iraq, who told us that in his country they made pierced almagda, from which one sucks the water, but however I never saw any in our land, nor did I ever read of it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almagda, so that those who do not know them may see them; and let them be properly of bronze:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let their heads be of this same subtlety, and the rear end in three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes various fleshy growths arise on the nose, of which some resemble scorpions with many feet; and there are some in which there is flesh ingrained with a livid color, and also soft flesh of a good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Then, in the case of this flesh which is soft and not ingrained, you must make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open his nostrils, and apply the oncin to that flesh, and pull it out; then cut what you can hold with a thin, sharp spatula on one side, until you know that all that flesh is removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if anything remains that cannot be cut, then operate with one of the subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if pus or an abscess forms, treat it as necessary; and if it is a malignant abscess, hasten and cauterize it until the blood is stopped and all the flesh is removed, then put eyewash and water or wine in the nose.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose opens and moisture comes down to the palate, know that it is healed; and if moisture does not flow as it should, know that there is flesh grown on the bone above, which the instruments cannot reach to cut: then you must put in a fairly thick linen thread, knotted at both ends, with a finger's breadth or less space between each knot; and let the patient put the end of the thread in his nose as far as possible, and pull it smelling until it comes out of the nose into the mouth; and often children in schools do this, and it is an easy thing for anyone who wants to do it; then hold the end that comes out of the nose in one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth in the other hand, and pull one after the other, sitting in front of the knots which are on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the knots have corrupted that flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nose as before; do this three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of the flesh; and then put a lead cannula in the nose for a few days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for cleansing the head, with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp, like a cannula, and lead it in likewise; and if you wish, make a closed cannula, and let the instrument be full to cleanse the head; and let it have a handle at the top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.
