Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to scrofula, then incise it as we have said in the incisions of scrofula, and if the wound discharges matter, then apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	Of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is broken, and the skin above is sewn, then often an abscess results, and the same happens with an inflamed and abscessed vein; and one recognizes it thus when it is due to the artery, the abscess is long and deep; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel a throbbing; and when it is due to the vein, it is round and clearly apparent; and it is foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits and in the groin and in the neck and in many other places, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, it is necessary to avoid the iron treatment, and the one who is in charge should avoid it as well, and in the one who has an arterial swelling, incise through the skin lengthwise; then open the incision with forceps, and carefully separate the artery from the tissues, until it is exposed; then place a needle underneath, and make it pierce to the other side, and draw out the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries in the temples; then puncture the area between the two ligatures with a lancet until the blood that is there comes out, and the abscess is emptied; then apply a treatment that draws out matter, until the ligatures fall off; then treat this with an ointment suitable for this, until it is healed; and if the abscess is due to the incision of the vein, then you must hold with your hand as much of the abscess as you can along with the skin, then insert the needle under the area that you hold with your hand, and make it pierce, and there be a double thread, so that you draw it from the other side; then ligate the abscess, as I have told you, tying one of two parts to the two ends of the thread; and if you fear that the threads will come loose, then insert another needle with a thread under the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and draw out the threads in four places; then cut the abscess until the excess comes out, then cut the excess of the heart and leave that which is ligated; then place a cloth moistened in wine and oil, then apply treatments of tents and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	Of the abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses occur in the artery and in the vein, abscesses occur in the nerves when they are injured, or by excessive work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and fingers and in all places where there are joints, and it is a severe abscess, and its color resembles the color of the flesh, and it is in many ways without pain; and when it is squeezed hard, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep in the body, but under the skin; and it moves well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, or down or up, and the one that is in the joints should not be cut with iron: perhaps contraction would result; and the one that is on the head or on the forehead, incise the skin with a small knife.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with forceps, and cut it at its root; and if it is large, lift it with forceps, and peel it off, then remove it and close the wound with sutures, and treat it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	Of the large hanging swellings
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in the abdomen and nowhere else, and it is a disease that is called "fungus" because of its resemblance, and its root is subtle, and its head large; and there are small ones and very large ones; and I saw a man who had two in his belly which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a thin root, and were split, and moisture constantly flowed from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them and found in one eighteen ounces weight, and in the other six and a half, and the procedure in the incision is that you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the little finger is white and moist and of subtle root; cut it with a wide small knife, and have the fire cautery ready.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the cutting, many times too great a flow of blood occurs, and if the blood overcomes you, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and afraid of the incision of the iron, take a well-made lead thread, and tie the little finger with it as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then restrain it, and do not cease to tighten the lead thread until it cuts the little finger, and falls off by itself without work; and if the roots are thick, there is fear in cutting itself because of the belly, but you can well cut half, then cauterize it so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and take care that you do not cut the little finger which is of a dark color and of poor sensation and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an infected abscess, and I will come to the treatment of cancer afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the swelling goes outside.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the swelling comes from cauterization of a wound or a fissure of the viscera, and is on the belly and some of the swelling comes out, as happens in other ruptures, or from blood flowing from veins or arteries according to what is in front, or from flatulence; and if it is due to the rupture of the viscera and the protrusion of the bowel, the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and opens with various discharges.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the protrusion of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it with one's fingers it retracts, and then returns, and perhaps it is healed, and it increases greatly at the entrance of the bath and through hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, and does not constrain; and if it is due to blood, the abscess appears large and hard through these signs, and is fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to flatulence, it is soft to the touch, and the work is that you look if the appearance is due to the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	Then you must leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, because of the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the bowel, then you must instruct the patient to hold his breath, and lie completely straight, then mark all around the swelling; then instruct him to lie often between your hands, then go around the place that you have marked with all the spatula, then stretch half of the abscess upwards with the large uncine; then tie it around with a strong thread, or a cord of strong silk firmly, and let the knot of the binding be loose; then open the half of the abscess stretched over the binding, and put your index finger in, and search for the intestine; if you find it caught by the binding, then untie it, and put the intestine outside the belly; and if you find the bowel, then take it with the uncine, and cut off the superfluity; and if the artery opposes you, or the vein, then go carefully around, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two strong threads in, and put the two needles around what you have done in a cross that you made pierce; then stitch the abscess in four places over the needles, and if you wish, remove the needles, and leave the place until it suppurates, and the dead flesh falls off by itself; or you cut it when it is thin and suppurated, then treat it as is necessary, and heal the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or the moisture that you find, then treat the place as is necessary, and close the place.
dou chancre	of the cancer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have described in the division the appearances of cancer, and how one should work on it with medicines, and how one should avoid the iron treatment; and we say that cancer grows in the marrow, and there is great caution in its treatment, and the ancients said that when cancer is in a place where it can be scraped away, such as cancer which is in the breasts, and in the thigh, and in similar places, and one should remove it entirely when it is in the beginning; and when it is large and old, then you should not approach it, for I never could heal any; nor did anyone ever heal any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operation, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile some times; then you have him bled if he has manifest repletion, then prepare the patient in a good place to perform the operation; then throw your uncines on the cancer, and scrape it from all sides, and remove it from all sides without leaving anything; and let the blood flow completely, and press well the place with your hand or with something, and if the flow of blood interferes with the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the blood is stopped; then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already said in the division the appearances of dropsy, and in what manner the collection of water is made, and the signs of each appearance, and the treatment which is done by medicines, and that which is treated by iron:  it is only ascites; and one should not touch with iron in these two appearances: that is to say, tympanites and anasarca, for it is a mortal thing; therefore when you treat this appearance of dropsy which is called "ascites" with medicines, and the treatment is not effective, then look to see if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness than dropsy, such as fever and looseness of the bowels and similar things; then do not touch him with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other illness than dropsy only, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should work thus: lift the patient straight up onto your hands, and pressing the abdomen, direct the water to the lowest part of the belly, then take the spatumile espinous according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be sharp on two sides.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	to a point, and yet let it not be so penetrating that it can reach the intestine when it is inserted, and cannot injure it; then see if the dropsy is gathered towards the intestines: then you must make an incision above the navel three fingers directly below the xiphoid process; and if the dropsy is due to the illness of the liver, then let your incision be on the left of the navel three fingers; and if it is due to the spleen, then let it be on the right, and it is not necessary that the patient lie on the incision lest the superfluities flow to that weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and push it in, and lift your hand with the whole spatumile between the skin and the peritoneum as if flaying to the quantity of a fingernail or thereabouts; then pierce the peritoneum until the spatumile comes to the empty place, and this is the place of the water, then draw it out, and insert this instrument of which here is the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a thin silver tube, and is of light bronze or brass, and has at the lower part one small hole; and on one side, three holes; and two on another side, and one on another; and the head is cut like a pen, and this is the form of the incision with which the scribes cut the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is the alemele, so that when the instrument reaches the water, it descends immediately upon the instrument; then empty half or a third part, for if you empty more than is necessary at that time, perhaps the patient will die from the dissolution of his vital spirit, or he will fall into a faint, or he will approach death; but empty according to the quantity of his strength, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's strength signify, and his pulse; then withdraw the instrument and retain the water, and it is retained immediately by the core which stops up the hole which is on the peritoneum, of which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then use the instrument again the next day, if you see the patient enduring this, and draw out a small quantity of water; do this every day, and take care not to continue until there remains only a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you are doubtful about the patient, and you leave much water in him, then treat him with hot sand or earth, and by much sweating or bathing and in the sun, and let him abstain from drinking; and treat him with drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stoppage of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who have no opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	Then it is necessary to pierce it immediately with a very fine spatula according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place a thin lead tube in the opening, and tie it and keep it thus for three or four days; and when he wants to urinate, let the tube be removed, and let him urinate, and then replace it; and perhaps it is not necessary, for the urine that comes forth will not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	For one whose opening is small, it is treated with the lead tube, as we have said, and it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the opening in its proper place are injured, for some are born who have the opening at the head of the penis, wherefore they cannot urinate forward unless they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot copulate because the matter cannot reach the penis, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies often on his back, then extend the head of the penis and cut it like the shaft of a feather, so that the opening falls in the middle, as it should; and guard against the flow of blood which often occurs there, and if it happens, staunch it with what staunchs blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often these warts appear on the penis, and are an unsightly appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; it is necessary that you take them with a sharp lancet, and cut and clean them all, then put on moistened cotton with Egyptian ointment; then treat it with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the wart is malignant, of a foul color and putrid, then you must apply cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it, and if the wart is on the head of the penis, and part of it is inside the skin and part outside, then you must remove the wart that is inside first; and when it is healed, then treat the outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, the head of the penis is not assured that it will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption come to his penis and to the testicle; it is necessary to remove all that which is black and corrupt, then apply a plaster of honey and flour made from pomegranate bark and vetches, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, apply lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	Cautery helps in two ways at once: namely, for the flow of blood and for the corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupt and retracted, then you must insert a lead cannula into the duct of the penis, and let the patient urinate through it; and when the skin is constricted at the head of the penis, which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or which happens due to a wound or abscess, then you must scrape it with a sharp instrument, until the constriction is loosened, and the head of the penis is freed on all sides; and if it is difficult to separate this, then you must scrape it with a spatula, a little from the head of the penis and the skin; then gently separate the two, and place a thin linen cloth moistened in cold water between them, so that it does not constrict again.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the separation of a continuous structure like other wounds; however, when we perform this operation of our own will, and especially on children, it is necessary that we perform the best operation and the one most conducive to healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not circumcise their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have nothing but what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the majority of masters and surgeons perform circumcision around a ring, and forcibly, and with a whole scalpel; the heart recoiled, for there are two membranes, and by chance one cuts the upper one and the lower one remains.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now it must be cut, and the pain is doubled, and the healing of the ring is not secure at the tip of the member; and in cleaning the nail, the iron sometimes slips, and the work is spoiled, and many times they are born thus that they have no need for cleaning, and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the cleaning which is done forcibly with the whole ligature of thread, I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forceps cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, you cut equally all at once; but let the thread be well tightened around the skin; and let the manner of the first operation be such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are only tying the thread around the penis, and then make him rejoice in every way you can; then make him stand straight between your hands, and place the forceps between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the penis and blow on the heart, and pull it upward until the head of the penis is in; then cleanse it well of the dirt that is gathered there, then tie the marked place with a double thread, then tie it below little by little another ligature; and hold it with two fingers for the second hour at the little finger and the index finger, and cut between the two ligatures, then remove the heart above quickly and pull the head of the penis; then let the blood flow little by little, for that is the best; and put powder on and on the powder a cloth glued with a yolk of a cooked egg tempered with rose water, mixed with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forceps for the cleaning is this: the two ends should be thin and sharp, and the ends should be as large as the handle equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in the cleaning is when the heart inside flees at the incision; then you must spread it with your fingernail, before the place forms an abscess; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, hold it with tongs, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if three days pass, and what is under the penis is swollen, leave it until the swelling of the abscess is subsided, and lightly scrape it; then cut it as much as you can move, and guard yourself from the part of the penis, it will not harm it at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the place of things like a suppurating wound with powder, which we have mentioned in the treatise on powders, and if one cuts the heart excessively, and it goes upwards, it will not harm; then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Of the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is from obstruction by stone, or congealed blood, or pus, or dead flesh, or similar things, which we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to a stone which is in or near the neck of the bladder, then the patient must be bent over on his knees; and his feet should be placed on his back, and he should stretch his belly from the part above his back, and the patient should restrain his breath as much as he can; and then the neck of the bladder is constricted to express the stone upwards, whereby the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with the instrument called a "syringe", of which this is the form: and it should be of fine silver, light as a bird's feather; and the shaft should be a palm and a half long, and should be slender at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the release of urine is that you take a double thread, and tie a little wool or cotton to the end, and put the end of the thread into the syringe; and cut off the excess wool and put it up to the tip of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg white, and have the patient sit on a seat, and moisten the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then bend the penis upwards towards the belly; then push the syringe forward to the bladder, and let the patient feel it coming to the empty thing, and this is not done in this order except because the passage where it goes is twisted; then gently pull the thread with the wool, and the urine follows the wool, then pull it out, and let the urine flow; and restart the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	Of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When excoriations or blood come into the bladder, or corruption gathers there, and you wish to instill waters and medicines, do it with the instrument called a "clepsydra," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the tip through which the medicine passes should be such that it well stops the penis without addition, so that one can draw out the moisture, and insert it when necessary; and when you wish to inject your medicines into the bladder, put the tip of the injector into the moisture, and pull on the plunger which is inside; thus you will draw the moisture into the injector, and then forcefully push the plunger in; thus the moisture will enter, and will immediately reach the bladder, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of the fine clyster with which one clysterizes the bladder: it is here:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or tin, and the tip is higher; and below there is a bag where the liquid falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put in it the liquid with which you wish to clysterize the bladder, then tie it between the two bags firmly with a good double thread, and slightly heat this liquid over the fire; then put the tip of the clyster into the penis, then press your hand on the bladder with all the liquid gently, until the patient feels that this liquid has reached the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make a circle of it, and pierce it round about; then put a strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a cup, and put inside what you wish of oil and liquid and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the liquid reaches the bladder.
de la piere	Of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already spoken in the division of the types of stone, and their extraction along with medicines; and I have spoken of the difference between the stone lodged in the kidneys, and all the signs, and in which stone one must operate by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is lodged in the bladder happens more often to children, and it is a sign that the urine leaps from the bladder similar to water in its subtlety; and gravel appears, and the patient scratches his penis, and urinates many times, and then it stiffens; and many of these have a prolapse of the rectum; and the healing of children is easy until they are four years old, and it is very serious in old men, and it is moderate in young men, in those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is first necessary to purify the patient with a clyster, to draw out all the bile which is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it sometimes hinders the finding of the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and lift him and move him downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes rises from the upper part; then make him sit between your prepared hands, and his hands should be under his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely inclined downwards; then seek and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, hasten now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall to the touch at all, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is a fully grown young man; and put it into his rectum, and seek the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, bring it to the neck of the bladder; then press on with your finger, and bring it to the outside where you wish to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and instruct him to lift the testicles upwards with his right hand, and with his left hand remove the skin which is under the testicles in the part where the incision is made; then insert the cutting spatula, of which this is the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And cut between that which is between the testicles and the rectum, not in the middle but on the side of the left buttock; and it should be directly over the stone, and your fingers should always be in the rectum, and let the incision be transverse so that it is wide outside, and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure of the finger which is in the rectum will make it jump out without effort; and know that there are stones which have angles and edges: they are difficult to remove; and there are those which are smooth, similar to an acorn, and round, whose removal is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	In the case of a stone with angles and edges, make a larger incision; and if it does not jump out, it is necessary that you use forceps which are like a file at the head, to grasp the stone so that it does not escape; or you insert underneath a thin curved instrument with a head; and if you cannot remove it in this way, widen the opening a little, and if the blood flows freely, staunch it with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, first bring the largest to the neck of the bladder, then cut into it, then pull it out, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are several.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it must be sawn, and a larger incision made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine constantly leaks because the wound cannot heal; but nevertheless strive to pull it out, or to break it with forceps, until you extract it in pieces; and when you have completed your work, fill the wound with incense, aloes and dragon's blood, and staunch it, and put over it a cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then raise the patient up to his neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie it, wash the area very well with oil and water, then treat it with diafinicon ointment and basilicon ointment, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot abscesses and corrosions appear in the wound, and blood clots in the bladder, and the urine is thereby retained, which is known in such a way that blood flows with the urine: then put your finger into the wound, and extract this blood, for if it remains, it will corrode the bladder, and rot it; then cleanse the wound with water, vinegar, and salt, and help it in every way you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that every time you treat it, you bind his two thighs together, and apply the medicines to the area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethra, and lodged inside, and the urine cannot pass; treat it as I said before, that you incise it many times, and one is excused from the operation by this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron drill according to this shape and let it be fitted with three angles into a firebrand:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the stone, so that it cannot return to the bladder; then gently insert the drill into the penis, until it reaches the stone; and turn the drill in your hand against the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; then the urine will come immediately, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then it is immediately broken, and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie one thread below the stone and another above, then cut the penis towards the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	Of the women's stone
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a stone is generated in women, and if it happens sometimes, the treatment is difficult, and it is forbidden for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a knowledgeable woman who reveals herself to the doctors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third reason is that perhaps one cannot find a knowledgeable woman in this art; and the fourth reason is that the stone of the woman is deeper than the stone of the man, wherefore a deeper incision must be made, and there is great fear. And if necessity demands it, then you must take a knowledgeable midwife, and one scarcely finds one, and if you do not find one, then seek a subtle, chaste doctor; and present to her a wise woman in the ways of women, or a woman who knows some part of the art, and instruct her to do what you instruct her concerning the investigation of the stone; and look very carefully if the woman is a virgin: then she must insert her finger into the rectum and search for the stone; and if she finds it, then she should compress it beneath her finger, and instruct her to place her finger in the vagina of the patient, and press her left hand firmly upon the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, then she must move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder downwards, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut above the stone at the root of the thigh towards the middle of the vagina, where it is usually found, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her finger above or below the stone, and let the incision be small at first; then put the instrument into the incision, and if you feel the stone, enlarge the wound so that the stone can come out, and know that there are many kinds of stones: that is to say, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and some which have roots.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Know the symptoms to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood overwhelms you, put crushed vitriol on the place, and hold it for an hour until the bleeding is stopped; then return to your work, until the stone is out, and have the instruments that I have described to you in the extraction of the stone in men to aid you in your work; and if the blood overwhelms you, and it is from the artery that is cut, put the powder on the place and staunch it with tampons and bandages, and do not attempt this again, and leave the stone and do not remove it, lest the patient die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is subsided, and the place is cleansed, then return to your work, until the stone is out.
de hernie carnouse	Of fleshy hernia.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Watery hernia is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white membrane, which is beneath the covering of the testicles, which contains the testicle; and it is called "membrane," and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the testicle, so that one thinks that it is another testicle; and it is the skin of the testicle between the white membrane that we have mentioned; and this only happens rarely.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this hernia is from weakness that comes to the testicles, and this matter is spread.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from a blow to the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: or it is a color tending towards jaundice, or it is without redness, or black, or watery white, and this happens more; and these are the signs to know this collection, for if it is in the white membrane that we have mentioned, then the abscess is round, somewhat long like the shape of an egg, and the testicle does not appear, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the proper membrane, then the abscess is round with a part of the testicle, and for that reason one thinks that it is another testicle; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white membrane, then one feels it well; therefore when you wish to know the color of the moisture, probe it with a completely small probe, of which the form is given above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to that then which comes after the probe, judge that which is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we cure it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be bled according to his strength and the repletion of his body; then lay him on his back, on something a little high, and put many cloths underneath him; then sit on his left, and command the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the penis to one of the two sides of the heart of the testicles; then take the sharp scalpel, and cut the skin of the testicles lengthwise up to near the root, and let your incision be completely straight in dividing the skin of the testicles up to the white membrane, and scrape it subtly according to your ability; then pierce the membrane full of water with a wide opening, and draw out all the water, and then apply your ointments, and extend the membrane upwards; and do not touch the heart of the testicles, but only the membrane; cut all around or in pieces, always on one side subtly, because if you do not cut it very skillfully, the water will return; and if the testicle jumps out from your work, put it back in its place when you have completed the work on the membrane; then bring together the two lips of the heart of the testicles with a suture, then treat it like other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the testicle corrupted by another illness, it is necessary that you tie the vessels which are suspensory, fearing the flow of blood; then cut the testicle with all the suspensory ligament, and extract the testicle, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if water is gathered in two parts together, know that these are two branches; then cut the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe the blood, and put in the wound wool moistened in rose oil; and put outside other wool moistened in wine and oil, and put over the two testicles, and put over it doubled cloths, and bind it all around with a bandage which is according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and fill them with lint according to this appearance and let them be joined by stitching at the opening of the breeches, and one of the ends should go over the buttocks to the back, and the other to the part of the root of the penis; and the other two ends over the two groins, and let all the binding be assembled in the loop of the breeches; and sometimes this branch is treated with cautery instead of an iron incision, and that is that you take a small, knife-like cautery, and cut the skin of the testicles, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white membrane which contains the water is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that membrane with the tweezers, and scrape it with this small, hot cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And cut it in all the ways that you can, until you have eradicated everything; and take care that the fire does not touch the testicle; and know that this operation is safer; and it guards better against the flow of blood, and is less dangerous than the operations of incision; and if anything contradicts you, a hot abscess or flow of blood or something else, then treat what contradicts you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful, and does not wish to undergo this operation because of its horror, then administer perforation, as I tell you, and that is that when you are certain by the signs that we have mentioned that a watery branch is there, then have the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the lower part with a wide spatula, and make the perforation along the length of the body; and let the hole be wide, so that all the water may flow out; then put cotton on the place, and bind it, and allow the rest of the water to flow, then treat it until the wound is healed; and if the white membrane does not allow the water to escape at the opening of the wound, then it is necessary that you insert a feather or the instrument with which one draws water from dropsical patients, the form of which is given above; and widen the wound a little, and know that the water will return, and will gather again after six months or thereabouts, and when it is gathered as before, and thus the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the incision of this branch there is fear in many situations, wherefore it seems to me that it is better to leave it; and I will tell you the operation and the appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come in the body, and especially in the testicles; and this is in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	That is to say, by a superfluity of acrid and watery humor, which is spread to the testicles, or from percussion; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and one finds no pain, and it is a serious abscess; and perhaps there are some serious abscesses, fearful and dangerous, and of a livid color, and sometimes comes from a rupture of an artery, or from an inflammation of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from a rupture of an artery, it is known by the disposition of a hot abscess, when you press it with your fingers; and you should not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	That which is made from inflammation of a vein is known by its disposition to expression from the touch of the fingers, and one can well make the incision on this type and on the other kinds; and it is that you cut the core of the testicles, then extend the testicle upward, and draw the matter from the white tunic, and free the suspensory ligament from all parts of the testicle.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the testicle is already soldered with the neighboring flesh, then it is necessary that you draw out the testicle, and cut it; and if it is adherent to the tunic, or to that which is within the vessels, it is necessary that you free all that matter, and cut it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the origin of the flesh is in the posterior location, it is necessary that you cut it all away, and extract the testicle, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, fill the wound with wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the testicles.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess enveloped in an envelope similar to a bud, with the softening of the testicles, and the patient moves painfully when he walks; and the cure of this illness is almost as frightening as the one before, and yet we will tell you the procedure, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a raised seat, then put the suspensory of the testicles down to your fingers, with all the vessels that are near the penis, and let the master hold them and stretch them strongly; then cut with a wide, sharp scalpel across towards the vessels until they are uncovered, and then peel on each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples; then insert a needle with double thread, and tie it at the first place where the pus has come, and tie it again at the other end; then cut them in half straight, along the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted moisture; then treat the wound like the others where pus is collected, so that no vessels are cut that nourish one of the testicles; for by this no harm comes, and if pus comes to all the vessels, it is necessary to remove the testicles with all the vessels; so that the testicle does not lose its nourishment because of the incision of the vessels, and dries up and cannot be healed.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the rupture of the spleen.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The occurrence of this rupture is by the section that occurs in the spleen, or the extension over the belly in the area of the flanks, because of which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the testicles; and this rupture is either of the spleen, or of its extension, and these two types come from many causes: from percussion, from jumping, from falling, from lifting a heavy weight, and from similar things; and the signs when it is from the extension of the spleen, are that it happens little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscess is equal to the depth, because the spleen presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are, when it is from the section of the spleen, that it causes a sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscess appears different, under the skin nearby, and that is because of the protrusion of the intestine and the body outside of the spleen.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.
