Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the head appears, it is necessary that you wrap around it a piece of lead of one and a half to two fingers' breadth, and tie it, and leave the lead hanging on the leg, and every time that a point comes out, wrap it around the lead and tie it; and if it is too long, cut a part of it, and wrap the remainder, and do not cut it at its root, until it is all out; for if you cut it, it re-enters the flesh, and causes an abscess and corruption in the place, and a bad illness; for which reason it must be treated little by little to the end, and nothing remains in the body; and sometimes this vein, when it is treated, is five palms long, or ten, and a man once came to me, to whom it protruded ten palms long, and when you cut it, put a probe in the opening, and probe it to the bottom, so that all comes out; and let the matter that is inside be emptied, and administer to the place medicines that prevent corruption for several days, then cure it like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein has many roots, and especially when it appears in the joint of the foot, or in the foot, and many openings come from it, from which pus escapes; cure it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of the worms that are generated between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land "ox disease," because it often happens to oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body ascending and descending, and one feels it well going from limb to limb, until it breaks the skin where it goes, and comes out; and it is engendered from the corruption of certain humors, just as worms, serpents, and lumbrici and ascarides come in the belly; and one doubts its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it ascends to the head, and it comes to the eye, perhaps it enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it to cure and draw it out, one can only extract it when it is moving: it is necessary then that you bind the place above and below with a strong ligature very tightly, then cut above and draw it out, and if the worm is deep in the flesh, and you do not find it, cauterize it with fire above, until it dies; and the greatest harm that it does is that it runs to the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming to the head near the eye, press the eyebrow strongly below it, then cut above, and draw it out; and the patient must use bodily cleansing with purgative medicines for the putrid humors, and abstain from foods that cause corruption.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called in our land "vakirir," and it is a pain that comes in certain limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I saw what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and a little afterwards, I saw it ascend like a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, like quicksilver when it runs from place to place; the pain departed from that place, and settled in the shoulder, and then a little afterwards ran throughout the body, until it came to the other arm; then she told me that it always turned around the body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very surprised how it moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this illness in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had seen many who had pain move from place to place, but I had not seen it as I saw it in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and uncovered veins, and therefore this constrained flatulence appeared; and it does not appear according to this reason in those who are plump, and who have moist bodies and full veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you wish to cure this illness, and the patient feels this pain, if it appears to you as we have said, bind it above and below quickly, and then cut above until that constrained flatulence issues forth from the place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, then cure it with that which expels flatulence, such as fetid pills, and pills of serapinum, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that there are those which have large points, and small, and barbed, and smooth; and those which have two angles, and those which have tongues, and those which are broken; and that which strikes in a limb strikes in two ways: either in a principal member, such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it then strikes in any place of these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you afterward, appear to you: then you must refrain from the extraction of this arrow, for death follows in many ways; and when these bad signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then draw it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow strikes there and pierces the bone, and the dura mater which is over the brain bursts, is when there is scotoma and swelling and dizziness and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps blood flows from the nostrils, or from the ears; and perhaps he loses speech and voice; and there flows from the wound white moisture resembling pus, and also something like shredded flesh; and if these signs appear to you, then refrain from treatment, and draw the arrow if it is not deeply embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of the arrow when it strikes the heart, are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were fixed in something hard, not empty; and perhaps the arrow moves like a pulse, and dark blood flows, and there comes coldness and cold sweat, and syncope: know then without doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign that the arrow has struck the lung is that frothy blood flows from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs deeply and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow strikes the covering of the chest, it is near the small ribs; and he breathes heavily and with great pain and sighs; and all the members of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow strikes the stomach, perhaps something of the undigested food comes out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes the belly, and some of the excrement comes out through the ruptured intestine, there is no hope of cure, nor of extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow strikes the bladder, and the urine flows out and comes forth, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the armpit and the spine of the back and the collarbone and the thighs and the legs, and similar members, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow struck him in the temple at the root of the nose: I probed it, and drew it out from the other side under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I drew out from a man an arrow that struck him in the fatty tissue of the eye beneath the eyelid; and the arrow was embedded, and I could reach only the point toward the shaft, and the arrow was as large as a Turkish bow, with a light iron head without barbs; the man was healed, and no ill effects came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was an Arabic one with barbs: I cut the barbs, and worked so delicately that I drew it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I drew an arrow from a man, which had struck him in the belly, and I thought that he would die; and after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change; I cut upon the arrow, and widened the wound, and drew it forth, and he had no ill effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And I saw a man whom an arrow had struck in the back, and the wound had closed over; and the arrow remained inside him, and he did not change his natural disposition, nor did he find harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I saw another man, whom an arrow had struck in the face, and the wound had closed; and it remained so without causing great pain; and many others similar.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I drew an arrow from a man of the king's princes, which had struck him in the nose, and was somewhat leaning towards the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded. I was called to treat it after it had been there three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I searched it with a very fine probe, and did not feel it; and he felt a prickling and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought that it was from the point of the arrow. I applied an attractive and digestive plaster to the place, so that the place would not swell; and the place of the arrow appeared to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I left the plaster there for several days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained thus for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his nose; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a sharp corrosive medicine to the wound for several days, until it was opened, and I probed it, and felt the head of the arrow which was sticking in the place; then I added to the opening of the wound with that sharp medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared to me visibly; and the time passed well for about four months, and then I widened the wound so that I put in the forceps, and moved it from one side to the other, but it could not come out; then I did not cease to refine and devise various instruments, until I grasped it one day with well-made forceps, according to what its form will become at the end of this chapter, until I pulled it out, and healed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the physicians judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I restored it then, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of certain arrows, so that you may apply your care to that which I do not say, for the book cannot encompass everything; but the wise master considers even a small thing well, and from that which is present and lacking to him, finds new work, and new instruments, for the handling of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not leave the limbs into which they are fixed except in two ways: either through the place where they enter, or through another place; and that which leaps out through the place where it enters, that is an arrow entering fleshy places, and sometimes leaping out immediately.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not leap out immediately, leave it until the flesh is rotten around it, and the exit is easier; and also if it is fixed in the bone, and it cannot come out, leave it so for some days, and move it each day; and then it will leap out, and if it does not leap out, pierce around it with a thin drill, until the place around is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is fixed in the bone of the head, and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned appear in the patient: do not pull it out, but leave it until it is loose after some days, for if the arrow reaches the meninges, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is fixed only in the bone, and does not reach the meninges, and the patient remains for some days without bad accident, then devise how to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply fixed and cannot come out, administer drills around it, as I have told you; then treat the place until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged in a part of the body so that one cannot see it, search for it with a tent; and if you feel it, pull it out with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot, because of the narrowness of the wound, and because of the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve or vein, widen the wound until the wound is large; and pull out the arrow if you can, and if the arrow has barbs by which it holds, remove the flesh that is fixed inside from both sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the barbs of the arrow, until you can pull it out; and be careful not to break the arrow, as you would find it harder to pull out.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot [pull it out] at once, leave it until the surrounding area is rotten, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood hinders you, administer what we have said in its chapter; and beware of cutting the nerve and the vein, and devise how you can best pull out the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient in the position he was in when the arrow entered him, for that is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot, place him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where something of it appears, or the skin is swollen where it is visibly or palpably felt: then cut above it until the forceps can grasp it, and then pull it out: it will come out immediately.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is lodged in the bone, rotate your hand round and round until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it again, and then resume the extraction until it comes out; and if the shaft of the arrow is there, pull it out with the whole shaft; and if the shaft breaks, and you wish to administer a push, use a hollow instrument, so that the point of the arrow enters the hollow of the instrument; and then push it out, and if the arrow is broken, use an instrument with a point entering in, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is poisoned, you must cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as is necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow breaks in the foot or in the belly or in the bladder or in the side, and it is close to the surface and you can cut above it, then cut; and be careful not to cut the vein and the nerve, and then pull it out, and then sew the wound, if necessary; and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps with which arrows are pulled is similar to a bird's beak, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead remover is like the feather of a bird, to push against the point of the arrow, as the form is here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the forceps for pushing and for pulling is here:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are 31 veins from which one is bled, of which 16 are in the head, namely: two beating veins which are behind the ears, which are called the two “herbech”; and the two arteries which are in the two apparent temples; and two veins which are in the two tear ducts of the two eyes, which are called “aspires”; and the vein which is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein which is at the root of the nose; and the two jugular veins which are in the neck; and the two veins which are in the upper lip, and these are the veins which are called “augeherich”; and two veins which are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, and is on the left side, and the lay people call it the “vein of the head”; and the middle one is called “faste”, and is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and the lay people call it the “vein of the heart”; and the basilic is on the right side, and the lay people call it the “vein of the belly”, and it is on the forearm, and it is that from which one bleeds, which appears manifestly on the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvatella is the vein which is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and in the foot there are three veins: one is below the bend of the wrist on the left side, and the second saphenous which is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein which is called “nesse”, which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	Bleeding from the veins which are behind the ears helps with old cataracts and migraines; and the quality of the bleeding, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then the patient tightens his neck with a bandage, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places hanging from the head: then seek them with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, bleed from there; then take the lancet, and put it under the vein down to the bone, then raise your hand with the whole vein upwards, and cut both the skin and the vein well two fingers across, and let out as much blood as you wish; then constrict and bind it, until it is healed; and I have already spoken of incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Bleeding from the two arteries which are in the two temples is good for old, severe migraine, and habitual ophthalmia, and for the flow of watery tears from the eyes; and the quality of the bleeding is as I say: and it is that the patient tightens his neck, until the two veins appear clearly; and feel the pulse under your finger, and then bleed from there; then raise the skin above the vein upwards with your index finger, and put the lancet underneath, and raise the vein upwards, and cut it, as you have done in the other two veins, and let the blood flow according to your need; then untie the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton; and then bind it tightly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken of their cutting and their extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Bleeding from the vein of the forehead is as good as bleeding from the cephalic vein for old facial diseases, and for migraine, and for redness; and the quality is that the patient tightens his neck by twisting, until the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called a "fossor", of which here is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and press down with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity that you wish; then untie the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is healed; and sometimes the work is done with a wide blade.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not necessary that the blade be too sharp; and bleed across, because the bone is near, and perhaps the blade will break when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Bleeding from the two veins that are in the two tear ducts helps the eyes, and ringworm, and redness, and hordeolum in the eye, and facial diseases; and the quality of their bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck by twisting with a bandage, as before; then bleed, and let the bleeding be across, a little bit of the length of the blade a little wide, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the blade is thin, perhaps it will break; then make the blood flow, as much as you need, and then bind it with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	Bleeding from the vein of the nose is good for fever, and raging thirst, and facial diseases, such as migraine and redness that comes on the face, and especially when it is old; and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck, then holds his nose with his left hand, and takes a long, thin blade, and inserts it between the lips in the space that is between the two nostrils, for the vein does not appear well there, and the blood will immediately begin to flow; and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it overnight, for it is very quickly restored; and this is the shape of the blade:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	Bleeding from the two jugular veins helps with shortness of breath, and the beginning of leprosy, and many diseases, and impetigo, and canker sores, and herpes, and fistulas; and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck under one and the other, as we have said; and let the master stand on the head of the patient, and the patient sits on a seat, then bleed the vein lengthwise a little widely, then draw blood moderately, or as much as is necessary; then do the same in the other vein, then untie the bandage, and bind both veins moderately, so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the bleeding of the lips.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Bleeding from the veins of the upper lip helps with ulcers in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and fissures of the lips, and of the nose and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the bleeding is to make the patient sit before you, and tighten his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, of which one is on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are known by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins: therefore cut one and the other, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, then cut the largest on each side, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of bleeding under the tongue.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Bleeding from the veins that are under the tongue helps after bleeding from the cephalic vein, and it is for the constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the uvula, and for diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient sits between your hands before the sun, and lifts his tongue, and looks underneath on each side for a black vein: bleed then one and the other, and do not go too deep, for underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the arm which are commonly bled are bled according to two methods: either by pricking with a lancet of one finger-width, or with a small olive-shaped instrument like a cutting knife, and it is called "anesil"; and they are wide and narrow according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the finger-width lancet is very renowned, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary for opening hairy veins full of thick apparent blood, and which contain thick and cloudy blood; and this is the form of the olive-shaped lancet:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtly pointed, and is for bleeding the subtle veins, where there is subtle, citron-colored blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	Bleeding from the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the abdomen; and it is necessary for the bleeder that he bleeds wisely, and that he guards himself from the artery which is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and a flow of blood comes, then he must stop it, as I have said; and the lancet should not be pointed, but cutting like a chisel.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica vein does not appear manifestly, then it is necessary that you search for it, and change to another; or you seek some branch of it, or you bleed in its place the vein in the middle of the arm: it appears manifestly; and cut it with the chisel-like lancet, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the place of the bleeding, then it is necessary first that you straighten the arm, that you touch the place until you know the pulse; then mark the place with ink, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with the chisel-like lancet; and beware that you do not strike the artery when you see the place swollen, for that is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it spurt upwards like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from the artery: hasten then, and put your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if the blood stops, which often happens; then bind the arm, and leave it so, and let not the patient move it; and let him be afraid, and not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped, and it overcomes you, and medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it appears, for the head of it retracts; and the blood stops.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a piece of bark of the spindle tree, and split it, and take one of the halves and bind it on well until the next day; if the blood stops, it is good; if not, then cure it, as we have said, with powders that stop blood; and the stopping is not difficult in many cases because of the smallness of the wound, and the binding power of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	Bleeding from the vein in the middle helps because it draws blood from the head above and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilica and the cephalic, as we have said; and it is necessary for the phlebotomist that he beware of the nerve which is below, and if he pushes too deeply, and he finds the nerve, and it swells and the healing is difficult, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve appears many times, and if it does not appear in some men because of its thinness, then it is necessary that you bleed it with the lancet; and avoid the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then cut it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	Bleeding from the cephalic vein helps because it draws blood from the head and helps the eyes; and it is necessary to bleed by pricking at the olive-shaped prominence or the myrtle-shaped prominence, for this is the safest of all the veins, for below it there is neither nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to seek the easiest place, and it does not harm if one misses the first time, and one starts again; and perhaps the place swells in some men when one misses the first time, but it does not harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bloodletting is according to your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it is only administered to preserve health and to avoid future illnesses; and the bloodletting should be done in one of the three veins that are in the arm: that is to say, cephalic, median, and basilic; and one should bleed at the beginning of spring while fasting, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of repletion appear; and one should bleed on the first day or the third, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bloodletting that is administered for illnesses has no determined time, but whenever there is need, day or night, at all hours and at all times; and one should not bleed children until fourteen years old, nor pregnant women except from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	And the elderly who have passed sixty years should not be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be bled, in whatever manner it may be, it is necessary that he cleanse the intestines with a light clyster, if he has much retained feces, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines the putrid superfluities harmful to the principal members; nor should one bleed someone who is too full of food, nor who is drunk, until he is sober, nor those with dropsy; and one should refrain from bleeding after colic, vomiting, diarrhea, and excessive intercourse with women, and from work, from wakefulness and fasting, and everything that diminishes the strength, either by something of the mind or the body; then thin the humors, if the blood is thick, by foods and drinks and by medicines, if you have the power; then enter the bath, if nothing prevents it, to thin the blood, and bleed from the vein of the arm around the third, as we have said; and guard yourself that day from work, and pain, and lust, and similar things; and be happy and joyful, and let the phlebotomist be higher than the one who is bled, and let him rub the arm two or three times, then tie the ligature above moderately, for when it is too tight or loose, the blood cannot flow; and then rub the place with the hands, until the veins swell, and one feels them; then let the phlebotomist moisten the lancet with a little old oil, then place the finger of his left hand on that vein below the place a little where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not flee and fail to be struck.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee like strings during bloodletting, and there are some that are full of wind, so that when one puts the lancet on, it withdraws from the lancet, and the vein cannot be opened, and so it is with those; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, therefore it is necessary that the phlebotomist be wise in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good; if not, then begin again a little below that place or above quickly, if the place is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the place is swollen, and the patient is frightened, leave it one or two days, and do not tie the arm: perhaps a hot abscess will come there; do not enter the bath, then resume bleeding if it pleases him; and if the opening is small, or the blood flows subtly and you fear that not enough blood will come out as you wish, strike in that same opening with the lancet straight; and work a little quickly, before the place is swollen; for this happens many times, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not resume bleeding, and put on a little oil of lily, for it lightens the body of the blood, and the lily is milder in this place than oil; and thus administer the oil of lily in every bleeding that you perform on the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and the same does triacle and ox-gall, when placed on the place; it thins the blood and spreads when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess occurs, which happens many times, especially when it is bled only once and the opening of the vein is small, hasten, and put on the place a sponge moistened in water and a little warm salt, and press it for an hour; and you must do this after the blood has issued from the vein, and if some blackness or greenness remains in the place after a few days, it does no harm; and if you wish, put on something of aloes or myrrh dissolved in juice of calamint, mint, or the like.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times an abscess and swelling occur at the bleeding of the basilica vein: then put your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of the hand, then that swelling is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid then putting on anything of what we have said, for perhaps blood from the artery will flow; but make a dry plaster to harden the place, then treat it with another treatment, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each person blood according to the quantity of his strength, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let so much out until it is red; and if you see it thick, let it out until it is thinned; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is full and strong, and needs bloodletting, that a larger wound be made for him, and the lancet be wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed him little and often, and one should bleed him by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of bleeding is safe from excessive bleeding and cutting of nerves, and is better than bleeding lengthwise or widely.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body fails during bleeding, it is necessary to give bread moistened in pomegranate juice; if he is feverish, draw blood three or four times. And if he is of cold complexion, let him eat before bleeding bread moistened in spiced syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during bleeding, after the loss of much blood, it is necessary that he drink broth of meat, and a subtle aromatic syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the section or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of a vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to bleed his arm again, and bleed another time, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he bleed little by little, according to the quantity of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to bleed his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, let him bleed seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to bleed from another place, should bleed on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body which is already heated, and causes fever; therefore it is necessary to draw a great quantity, and enlarge the opening until it flows in a stream; then you should observe all the conditions of bleeding, and put your hand on his pulse while he bleeds, that death may not come instead of fainting, and this happens many times, when the bleeder is negligent; and it is not necessary, when you wish to untie the arm and cause blood to flow a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press strongly upon it; nor, if it is curved, that you extend the arm hastily, for that would be bad; but leave it until it bleeds a second time; or you prick it with the point of a blade, until the blood which is congealed at the opening of the vein comes out strongly, and put on a little salt mixed with water, and press lightly upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not bind it, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if there is need to draw blood a second time, bleed him in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the middle of the arm is bled in place of the vein of the head because it is composed [of/with] it.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of bleeding is that the patient puts his hand in warm water until the vein is red; then it should be bound moderately, so that the vein appears well, then bleed it immediately across, not across the width or length; and let the opening be wide, and be bled quite close to the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot come out, put the hand back in warm water, and let the blood run into the water, until you have enough; and if it is in summer, do not put the hand back in warm water, for one puts it there more in winter than in summer; and the bleeding of this vein is safer than all other veins, because there is neither artery nor nerve there.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Bleeding from the vein of the right hand is good for all liver diseases, and this is the manner: bind the hand, and put it in warm water until the vein is swollen, so that one can see it; and bleed it across, and if you cut it completely through, it does not matter; and do not go too deep, because the nerves are underneath completely bare of flesh, and then put the hand back in warm water, if the blood is congealed in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn as much blood as is necessary, put oil and salt on the vein to heal quickly, and so do for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	Bleeding in the left hand is good for spleen disease, and do just as I have told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	Bleeding from the saphenous vein is good for all illnesses that are below the body, such as illnesses of the womb, and retention of menses, and illness of the kidneys, and of the old thighs and legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of this bleeding is that the patient puts his foot in warm water, and rubs the vein until it swells, and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot many veins go; bleed then in the largest vein, or at the ankle, which is more valuable.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bleed it on the foot, beware of the nerves that are underneath, and bleed it across as if cutting; and let the blade be sharp.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, put the foot back in the water, and let the vein empty well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the bleeding fails the first time, begin again the second time a little higher, for the place is salty; do not fear the nerve, as we have said, and so do with the saphenous vein of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the outer ankle, and bleeding it benefits the hip pain, when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of bleeding it is such that the patient enters the bath, and presses above the ankle with four fingers twisting, for otherwise the vein does not appear; and if it appears, bleed it in every way that you can, and across; and it is better that you cut it, for the place is salty, and it is very hidden in many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, bleed any vein that appears on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and draw as much blood as you wish, and then untie the ligature, and apply cotton and bandage it; it is then healed.
des sainies de ventouse	Of cupping bleeds.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cups are made of horn, or of brass, or of glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by cutting and drawing blood, or without cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is without cutting is done in two ways: either it is with fire, or without fire; and cupping which is done by cutting and by drawing blood is done in fourteen places of the body, of which one is on the very top of the head; and another is in the middle of the neck; and two others on the two sides of the neck; and the cup under the chin; and the cups on the two shoulders; and the cups on the buttocks; and the cups in the two arms; and the cups in the two legs; and the cups on the two ankles; and cupping does not draw blood except from the small veins which are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken one at all, as one does with vein bleeding; and it is not necessary that it be administered, neither with fire nor without fire, in any illness which comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of illness it is necessary to cup, or by custom, then we administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at any time; for there are some who, when they need cupping, have a heavy head; and there are some who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness in their eyes; and some who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and spit blood; and there are some who dream, and see at night blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we order it to be cupped after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	Bleeding from the nose helps the headache... that comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary that this be after the evacuation of the whole body; and this cupping is in place of bleeding from the cephalic vein, and it is not necessary that one who is of cold complexion use it, or who has catarrh, for this does them much harm; and therefore it is not necessary that the elderly use it, nor those who have cold illnesses in the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who bleeds often from the nose becomes forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to place the cup a little lower because of the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Cupping in the neck is in place of bleeding from the head and the basilic vein, and therefore it is good for tightness of the chest, and for a fissure in the lung canal, and for cough, and for fullness; and it is necessary to apply it gently, for if it holds too firmly, it causes forgetfulness or stomach and heart problems.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Cupping at the two ribs of the neck is good for headaches, and ophthalmia and migraine, and for strangulation, and for pain at the roots of the teeth, and is in place of bleeding from the basilic vein; and it is necessary that you instruct the bleeder that he carefully place his hand, that he not cut the artery, and that there be no excessive flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	Cupping under the chin is good for mouth disease, and for corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in place of bleeding from the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Cupping of the shoulders is good for illness that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Cupping of the elbows is as good as bleeding from the three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the bleeder that he not cut too deeply, for the place is thin of flesh, and has nerves and arteries underneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass which is placed on the buttocks is good for hemorrhoids of the fundament, and for lower diseases, and it is necessary that the cupping glass be large, and be of bronze, that it may draw well; and perhaps, if it were thin, it would break; and it makes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Cupping of the legs bleeds profusely, for they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains of the loins, and of the womb, and of the bladder, and they restore the menses; and they are in place of the two saphenous veins, and of the two ankles, and yet they weaken the body after long use, and cause fainting in many constitutions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the cupping glass is that you first place it empty, and suck moderately, and apply it quickly, and move evenly, and do not cease doing this, until you see the place red and swollen, and the redness of the blood appears; then cut, and reapply the cupping glasses, and take heed to the constitution of the body, for there are some who have tender flesh, and clear pores: then it is necessary to cut only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and somewhat deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to cut twice: the first time to make finer the passage of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to cut a third time; and when we wish to draw blood little by little, then once is sufficient for us.
