Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want much blood, we begin again often; and if the blood is thick, cut deeply, and the limit is that the skin should be pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the places of the cupping glasses with an aperitive and dissolving oil: if it is in summer, with violet oil, or almond oil, or gourd seed oil; and if it is in winter, with cress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or another similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is thick and cold, take marjoram oil, or balm oil, or dill oil, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one whom one heals has tender flesh and large pores, then it is not necessary to put any oil there, but it is necessary to wash it after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or gourd water, or porcelain water, or another similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, let him rise with vinegar, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have thick superfluities rise with old wine, or beet juice, or decoction of dill or chamomile, or others similar; and it is not necessary to cup before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath one or two hours; and do not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he be warned when he should be cupped and when he is cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware if the one whom one heals is choleric, and if the blood is too sharp and inflamed; then it is necessary that he take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces with vinegar, and similar things; and eat chickens, and capon meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion, let him take honey syrup, and moderately fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat chickens and small birds and pigeons; and the day that he will be cupped, he should drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give to some men sometimes theriac or nutmeg before cupping, or after, to strengthen the principal members; and let the blood be thinned, but it is not necessary that those who are hot drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cupping glasses which are applied without cutting are those which are applied to the liver, and to the spleen, and gout, and to the belly and the udder and the kidneys and the hip, for these members do not tolerate being cut upon, and it is only done to draw blood from one member to another, such as we apply to the breasts when a woman nurses; to remove the viscosity which is in the member, such as we apply cupping glasses to the belly and to the udder to reduce the member; and it removes the pain, when there is obstruction or stone, and by its attractive virtue it perchance removes the obstruction, or dislodges the stone from its place; and thus it does when it is applied to the liver and to the spleen when there is retained flatulence, and these cupping glasses are administered empty to only suck; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes full of warm water, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in such a manner that one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled for this purpose.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass administered with fire is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And let it be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and let it have on the side around the middle a small hole, as to insert a needle, and let it be of brass, smooth in front so that it does not injure the patient when placed on the member; and let it have in the middle a crossbar of brass or iron, to place a burning candle in, and let there be large and small ones according to the illnesses and the age of those who receive them; for the cupping glasses of children are different from those of the old, and of the thin from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should thus apply this cupping glass to the member: take the candle of wax or a liniment, and place it in the cupping glass across the bar which is in the cupping glass, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping glass so that it does not burn the patient; and then place it on the member, and your fingers should be on the hole that we have mentioned, so that when you wish, the vapor escapes, and you remove the cupping glass; and you take the liniment as before, and repeat it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping glass then, which is administered in the illness of pleurisy, with water, there is no bar or hole, and it is only administered when it is full of water, and it is placed on the member only; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leeches are only administered in members where cupping glasses cannot be placed because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in places denuded of flesh, such as a finger or nose, and others similar; and the qualities of the use are that when you find leeches which are in clear fresh water without putrefaction, you take them; and you place them for a night in fresh water, until they are hungry, and have nothing in their bellies; and then let blood be drawn from a vein and with a cupping glass, then rub the member until it is red, and apply the leeches; and when they are full, and fall off, if it is a place where one can apply a cupping glass, apply it, for this is very worthwhile afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, raise the place with vinegar, and then with water, very well, and then wipe it; and if the place bleeds too much after the bodies of the leeches, soak a linen cloth in cold water, and apply it, until the bleeding is stopped; and if the bleeding is profuse, apply crushed vitriol, or galls, and similar things, until it is stopped; or you apply to the place halves of peeled beans, and leave them until they stick to the place, this will stop it immediately; and if you need more, take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the leeches do not want to attach, rub the place with fresh blood, or prick it with a needle until blood comes out, and then apply them, and as soon as they smell the blood, they will attach; and when you see that they are falling off, sprinkle a little aloes and salt, crushed, or ashes, on them, and they will fall off immediately.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that foolish men avoid this chapter, because they have never seen any of the ancient books, nor read any letters about it; and for this reason the science is diminished in our land, for I never found any good ones; and I know nothing about it, except through the science of the ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have drawn the science from it, and by experience, and by the custom of my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained, and have shortened it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in the two chapters above.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary then that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the text and the chapters where the wise man sets his understanding, and dwells on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture, dislocation, sprain, or contusion occurs to someone, it is necessary that you hasten to bleed the patient on one side and the other, if nothing prevents you, such as weakness of body, or a child, or an old man; or if the weather is not very warm, or too cold; and let him eat cold foods, that is to say cold dishes, and the flesh of birds and of young deer, and let him not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and let him not overfill himself with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of a hot abscess, or of the spread of matter to the limb; then let the patient return to his former regimen that he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one nourish the patient with foods that provide substantial nourishment, or that have viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and heads, and feet, and cow's paunch, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment, the flesh is restored and the fracture heals sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of old and decrepit people cannot be well restored or healed according to their nature because of the dryness of their limbs, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but there is a cure, reset the broken bone with strong bandages that support and join the limb together, until it strengthens as it was before; and do not hinder its work, and therefore it must be nourished with strong foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a fracture of the head is different from a fracture of the breast, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes transversely, and another obliquely, like the cut of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with only a small fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each type has its own device and its own instrument in its restoration, according to what comes back into its place; and a fracture of the bone is known because the place is twisted, and it appears clearly from without, and sounds when pressed by the hand; and when there is no twisting or sound to the touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but there can well be twisting, or fissure, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	Then you must not move it with your hand, but apply the medicines that come next, and then extract it very subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that in a fracture that goes transversely, and the two parts are disjointed, you must immediately put them together equally, so that hot abscesses do not form; and if hot abscesses form, leave it a few days, until the abscesses are calmed; then put it together carefully and skillfully, and know that its restoration is easier than the restoration of one where there are pieces; then extract it, as is appropriate below.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone has broken pieces, extend it from two sides, if it is a hand or foot, or with your hand if it is a small limb, or with two cords, or with one cord and your hand; and put the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, bring back all the parts to their places as best you can, and take care that your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient; and join the two ends of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And you will feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not well: then straighten it nicely, and do not tighten it too much, nor press it as those do who cause hot abscesses and contractions in the limb by their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, strongly instruct the patient not to move it, neither while awake nor while sleeping, nor by turning, nor in any other way; and ensure that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels any pain, it is not in place, and it must be put in such a position that it feels no pain; and ensure that it is put straight, so that no tortuosity comes when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and in size and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers and similar:  it is necessary to wrap them with soft and fine linen cloths; and those that are large, such as thigh and leg: it is necessary to wrap them with a wide and firm bandage, because the wide bandage embraces the whole large limb, and tightens it equally on all sides, so that there is no slack; then tie around light tow, three or four turns according to the limb, and tighten your hand a little around the whole bandage, then go above the fracture and tighten less, so that the fracture then moves the fracture a little; and soften the bandage little by little, until you take a large part of the healthy place, then take another bandage, and turn it again over the fractured place; then go to the part below the fracture, and tighten it moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first book above; then put between the bandages linen tow or cloths, until it is all even, then tie all over it a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or abscess, then put on something that soothes a hot abscess, and which removes the swelling, and leave it so for some days; then tighten your splints, and let them be half of a wisely sawn wide cane, or of wood from which one makes wedges, or of palm branches, and let them be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but it is necessary that the splint that one puts on the fracture be a little thicker and wider than the others; and let it be as long as is necessary for the limb in smallness or size; then tighten over the splints as you did in the first book, then tie over a thread suitably, as in the first book over the fracture; tighter above, always less; and it is necessary that the threads be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of the fools who make their bandages of twisted linen cords, and that is a great error, for the bandage cannot be even if it is too subtle, and it is not necessary that there be between each splint less than a finger's breadth of space.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the ends of the splints after the tightening in healthy places, then put under them linen tow, or carded wool, so that he does not get hurt.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the skin is broken, I will tell the treatment afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to tighten splints on all broken limbs the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, it is not necessary to put on tight splints before five days or seven, or more according to your certainty of a hot abscess arising; and here is the manner of the ancient plasters for restoring fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and it is that you take the flour that sticks to the walls of the mill, and cook it with plenty of egg, and put this confection, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common manner of the plaster restoring the fracture in many conditions, and especially for women and small children, for it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restoring fracture and dislocation and torsion: take 3 drachms of bdellium and ladanum and enula and asafoetida and gum arabic and myrrh, each 10 drachms; myrrh and aloes, each 5 drachms; elecampane 9 drachms; and make them into powder, and mix them with plenty of egg; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth much to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of plaster that is good for torsion: take myrrh and mallow, each 10 drachms; myrrh and aloes, each 9 drachms; acacia 6 drachms; Armenian bole 10 drachms, and grind well, and cook with water or plenty of egg, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another manner of plaster for joints and bones separated from their place, and soothes the pain arising, and the grating of the bone, and the fracture: take new wool, and moisten it in vinegar and cooked oil, and put it on the place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore, but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and properly removes the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of plaster which restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves, and leaves of henbane, and grind together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another manner of plaster for the restoration of a bone fracture and to lessen the remainder of an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take marshmallow root, chamomile, violet flowers, bean flour, one part of each; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is heated, mix it with moist coriander water, or with water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another manner of plaster stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take marshmallow roots, and flaxseed, alkanet, melilot, and comfrey, and violet and chamomile flowers, of all equally one part; and grind, and mix with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put on a broken limb for restoration except a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and says that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should put on the broken limb, for restoration, slightly warm dry things, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of plaster that is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and chopped human hair, or bird feathers, and marshmallow, and equally, and grind them, and make a plaster and bind it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then unbind it a little afterwards, and take care if the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; if not unbind it for several days. And if pain or itching comes to the place, without rest or swelling, then hurry, and unbind it, and remove the plaster immediately; and take a light cloth, and a wet sea sponge, and dip it in water, and lift the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is calmed; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry wool, moistened in water or rose oil, and bind it on a nut, until you are sure of a hot abscess; and the inflammation of the limb is calmed, and the pain is gone, then begin again the subtle binding, and a little plaster, and do not bind it so tightly as before; and continue until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that hot abscess and redness and pain and swelling are completely gone, and you need a plaster and binding, then begin again, as you did before equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the limb, then do not unbind it before three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes leave it twenty days, according to what one sees, until the fracture heals, and the joining of the flesh approaches; then bind it more tightly than before, and thicken its flesh, as I have said before; and if you see the place drying more than is necessary, know that nourishment cannot come to it; then sprinkle it with warm tepid water, every time you unbind it, and that should be every third day, and loosen the binding a little; by this work then nourishment comes to the limb quickly, and quickly amends what the foolish physicians do, who restore the limb forcefully: this is bad, and it is dangerous work, and I see nothing else but leaving it and working correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the various kinds of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of fractures, and diverse forms, and the causes are different; for there are fractures that are made by the blow of a sword, and the neck breaks the bone all the way down to the spongy bone which is under the bone, as an axe or a club does; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called "hachure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts the bone from above without piercing, and this kind of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a blow from a blunt object, or a fissure, or from a blow from a stone, or from falling on a stone, or from other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture, which reaches down to the membrane which is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound which is as fine in the bone as a hair, and the fissure is small, and for this reason this fracture is called "capillary"; and if the wound which is made either by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by a similar thing, and makes the piece of bone enter below, and the place is swollen as caulkers do when they strike on cauldrons; then the stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have moist bones in the head, like the heads of children; and it happens in all these kinds of fractures that small pieces are separated like stars; and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all kinds of fractures by the pulling on them, and the probing with probes, and by the corrupted flesh which is on top.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary resemblance is known by this, that when one has uncovered the bone, and one rubs gently on it, the black fracture appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, take heed of the accidents of the patient, and if you see any bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of consciousness, and convulsions, and swooning, and acute fever, and the eyes protruding and reddening, and other similar things in several dispositions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no frightening accident, and you hope for healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded man first comes to you, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day, if you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, before the flesh under the bone is corrupted, and the accidents that we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the membrane that covers the brain, then it is necessary that you split the split part thus: and it is that you take the head of the wounded patient, and uncover the bone in all the ways that you can, and upon the surface of the wound as gently as you can, and if bleeding occurs upon uncovering the bone, or a hot abscess, help him with what is necessary, and it is that you fill the place with cloths soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the hot abscess is calmed, and you are assured of the cessation of bleeding; then begin to remove the bone around it, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method is that you cut with a narrow incision in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then put another incision there, larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have a number of different incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and be of tempered iron; and work lightly, so that you do not injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and hard, then you must pierce it around, before you apply incisions with trephines, not so deeply that they pierce beyond the skull bone, and it should have a rim or a circle above the point, which prevents the point from passing beyond the bone; and you must have several, so that each comes to its place in the thickness of the bone, so that you have trephines for all the head; and this is the form of the three types of trephines:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The method for piercing around the fractured bone is that you place a trephine on the bone, and turn it with your fingers until you know that the bone is pierced; then place the trephine elsewhere a little further on, and do so all around, then cut with the incisors the piece of bone which is between the holes, and do this as delicately as you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you extract the bone with your hand, or with some of the instruments that you have such as forceps, pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the dura mater.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and removed the bone, you must smooth the remaining bone fragments with another instrument similar to an incisor, but it must be thinner and sharper than the other incisors; and if any small bones or scales remain, remove them gently with one of the instruments; then treat the wound with tents and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of operation is that which Galen mentions, which is safer; and he praises it highly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture appears, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place under the head of this lenticular incisor, of which this is the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the sharpened part is on two sides, so that the cutting edge is towards the bone; then strike gently with a small mallet, so that you cut the bone all around, and take good care of the membrane that is underneath; if it is adherent to the bone, remove it gently, for it is easily removed without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not reach the membrane, and the bone is only cut on the surface, and there are small pieces, then you must remove those roughnesses, and remove the splinters with a fine rasp, of which you should have various sizes, to use in each place the most suitable, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Begin first with large rasps, and then with finer ones, and do not cease doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair-like incisions and subtle fractures, you must apply a remedy according to its condition; and this is something not easily explained to one who has not studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the dura mater is exposed, you must take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled over two or three times, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth; and do this as gently as you can, so as not to injure the dura mater, then apply another bandage over it, and do not bind it tightly, only enough to hold the wound; and leave it like that for one or two days, until the inflammation of the abscess is reduced, then unwrap it, and apply medicines such as lily roots, bean flour, incense powder, birthwort, and similar things; and make a powder of these things, and place it on the wound, and always apply cleansing medicines without causing irritation; and ensure that the wound is always clean, that you do not leave ointment on it, nor let pus accumulate, for when pus accumulates on the brain membrane, it corrodes and rots it, and great harm comes to the patient; for when something irritating is placed on the dura mater, it causes necrosis on top.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if any bad accident befalls the patient, as we have said, it is undoubtedly doubtful.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackness comes only because of the medicine that has been applied, which has such a quality, you must take one part honey and three parts rose oil and glue a cloth, and put it on the dura mater; then treat it in the manner of treatment that is necessary, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one alone, for these are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it is crushed or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must put your little finger in the nostril, and set the fracture in place with your index finger and your little finger outside, until the nose returns to its natural shape; and do this gently, and ensure that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper part of the nose, and the finger cannot reach the place, you must set it with the head of a slightly thick rod.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is in two parts, do likewise, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the inflammation is subsided, then place in the nose tents of linen cloths, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you place one on the other side, if the fracture is there; and let the tents be so large that they fill the nostrils.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say that one should moisten the tents with butter, and change them each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but they should be moistened in a confection of egg white and mill dust; then leave the tent until the bone is firm, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one puts goose feathers in the nose instead of tents, and there is a soft cloth around, and it holds the fracture, and the patient blows through it; now do what you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if hot abscesses come to the nose while you are working there, put cerote or cotton moistened in rose oil, or a little diachylon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses do not come there, put a plaster on the outside, of barley flour and incense powder, mixed with egg white, then put light tampons on it, and do not bind the nose; and if the fracture of the nose is small, and it is broken into small pieces, extract it with instruments suitable for this, then sew the fissure, and treat it with things that generate flesh and heal, such as plasters and ointments suitable for this; and if there is no wound inside the nose, treat it with tents, and put lead weights on it until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the fracture of the mandible.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is broken underneath, and there is no wound outside, and the fracture is only outside, and it is not broken in two, except for splinters inside, one recognizes it easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is in the left mandible, put your index finger of the right hand, and put the fracture inside gently, and set it with the other hand from the outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is separated into two, it is necessary that you administer extension from two parts, until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth occurs, or fracture, then bind them with a gold or silver or silk thread, then place cerote on the broken mandible, and place a double cloth over it; and place on the cloth a well-made large star, or a piece of even leather, long and wide according to the mandible, and bind it as tightly as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the shape changes, unbind it on the third day, and then reset what has changed; and apply a plaster, of mill dust with egg white or bean flour, after you have removed the cerote; and place light wool over the plaster, and if the plaster dries, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it is healed; many times it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if hot abscesses come, administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is fracture and wound together, observe if any piece of bone is removed; if so, carefully remove it with the instruments suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with a flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, sew the wound, if it is large, and apply suitable plasters to it, to generate flesh, until it is healed.
de la forcele	Of the collarbone.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The collarbone breaks often in front, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is in three ways: or it is broken and separated in two, and there are pieces, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedure, when the fracture is without a wound, is that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the broken collarbone is felt; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then set the fracture with your fingers, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor unevenness.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place under the patient's shoulder a round sphere of cloth or wool, and let it be large according to your need; and extend and lift the collarbone, and pull the sphere with your hand, so that you set the fracture evenly, as is necessary.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the end of the collarbone outwards, because it is deeply embedded, then it is necessary that the patient lie often on his back, and place under the shoulder a medium-sized pillow, and let the assistant lower the shoulder, until the collarbone is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then set the fracture with your fingers, and if you find it shattered, then you must incise it; and pull out the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join due to any obstacle, then cut it with one of the scalpels you have; but place this instrument under the collarbone to protect the soft tissues:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it resembles a spoon, and is not sharp, and should be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the nature of the work; and it has two ends, as you see, and one is wide, and the other narrow, as is the opening of the wound that you have made when you pulled out the bones; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, sew up the wound, and if the opening is small, or you fear a hot abscess, fill the wound with lint and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses appear, moisten a piece of lint in rose oil, vinegar, and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The binding of the bone, when it is without wounds and cuts, is that you apply to the bone a plaster of powdered millstone and egg white, and place light tampons on top, and place a splint under the armpit, if you need one; then take a very wide bandage, a handspan wide, then place a double layer of cloth over the tampons and the plaster; then take a thin strip of three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the end of the bandage hangs down; and place the strip over the fracture, and turn the bandage over the neck and under the healthy armpit, and under the affected armpit; and tighten it on each side, and when you see that the binding holds the fracture properly, and you clearly see that the strip does not move over the broken bone, then check it every day, and when the binding loosens, tighten it; and make the patient lie on his back, and place a small pillow under the armpit while he sleeps to raise the shoulder; this will ease the fracture of the collarbone by raising the shoulder, or you bind his arm to his neck, and do not unbind it unless a bad accident occurs, for up to twenty days; then renew the plaster, if you see that it is needed, and tighten it and leave it like that, until it is healed; and it is healed in at most twenty-eight days, and in less time for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the fracture of the shoulder.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It rarely happens that the shoulder breaks at the wide part or in the middle, and it is only known by touch;  then adjust it according to the nature of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural shape, in all ways that you can; then put on the place powdered millstone with egg white, and light tampons, and place a double layer of cloth on top; then place on top a wide and thin strip, a little wider than the shoulder, and if under the strip there is hair in any place on the shoulder, fill that hair with linen tampons, so that the strip fits evenly; and then bind it tightly with a strong bandage, so that the strip does not move from its place, and check the binding every day; and every time it loosens, tighten it, and reposition the strip if it is out of place, and let the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder is healed in twenty or twenty-five days. And when this number of days is complete, unbind it, and be sure, for it is not a bone that easily displaces.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone protrudes, and points below the heart, then incise it and remove it, and do what we have said in the fracture of the collarbone to calm a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	Of the fracture of the breastbone.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The breastbone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it inclines downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and shortness of breath, and coughing, and perhaps vomits blood, and the hair appears in the broken bone, and one feels it well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back, and a cushion is placed between his shoulders, then press the shoulders, and bring together the ribs of the two sides with your hands, and subtly put it evenly in all ways that you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then put on plasters and lint over it with a fine layer of salt, or other light wood, and wrap it in a cloth, and bind it over the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turn the bandage round to the back, and tighten it well, and check every hour the bandage, and if it loosens, then tighten it; and if it is necessary to unbind it, because of corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hasten, and unbind it, and remove the plaster, and treat what has come there by means of cures; then reapply the plaster, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of the ribs.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of the ribs only occurs in the thick parts behind the back, and at the front; and they only bend because they are slippery; and one feels it well by examination with the fingers.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you set the fracture evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bind it tightly, with a bandage, if you need one.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is inward, the patient feels very great pain, and a stabbing pain, as from pleurisy, because the bone pierces the lung; and he breathes with difficulty, and quickly vomits a great quantity of blood, and this is a serious condition, and the ancients have put great ingenuity to it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And some say that it is necessary to administer foods that inflate the belly, to push the fracture outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, lest hot abscesses arise, if they have not already appeared.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have appeared, then heal them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that one places cupping glasses on the spot, to strongly draw out [humors], and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cupping glass might attract superfluities to the place due to the weakness of the constitution.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that one should cover the area with wool soaked in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to evenly distribute the poultice around, then it should be treated with the treatment for pleurisy, with food and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear because of the bone that pierces the flesh, and there is doubt for the patient, then it is necessary to cut open above the area of the broken rib, and it is necessary to place an instrument underneath to protect the viscera; and then one must cut the bone and draw it out slightly, and then stitch the two edges of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess appears, then apply cloths soaked in rose oil to the area; and treat the area meanwhile as is necessary for an abscess, and let him lie often on his side where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	Of the fracture of the neck.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes a fracture occurs in the bones of the neck, and it rarely happens that it bends; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, then observe if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and he cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many ways, and if he moves them and feels well when they are pulled and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and that the patient will be cured, if treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, then observe if his feet are softened, and if the symptoms are there which are in the hands, and on his back there is flatulence and involuntary defecation; and when he is turned on his belly, involuntary defecation occurs.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is turned on his back and he wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that he is mortal: therefore do not labor in his treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these symptoms do not occur, the condition is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you observe if there is a hot abscess, then apply rose oil or egg yolk oil to the spine until it is calmed; then apply one of the strengthening and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on the part where he feels pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is separated, it is necessary to cut over the heart; and remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then treat it with an ointment generating flesh, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "cow's head", put your little finger of your left hand there, and set it even with the other hand as best you can, then apply the plaster and the bandage on top, if you need it; then restrain it, and if there are separated bones, cut and remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it happens, it is only a slight lessening at the head; and it cracks lengthwise, and inclines inwards, and the patient experiences pain at the site, and throbbing, and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.
