And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, until you are over the fracture; and know what the fracture is and its shape; and if the fracture is only at the head, then set that fracture, until it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is lengthwise, or it inclines inwards, make the patient lie on his stomach, until the resetting of that fracture is prepared for you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it evenly, apply the plaster, then place a splint of wood or horn, and bind the fracture so that it does not move; and fill the space under the ribs, so that the sides are even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if a hot abscess develops there, do not touch it until the hot abscess is subsided, and apply what we have said before; and then return to the resetting, and bind it as is necessary, if there is no bad complication; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the fracture of the shoulder.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the side and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it must be restored according to one of two methods: one is that you take a straight piece of wood of medium thickness, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie two cords to the two ends, and hang them up, and the patient sits on a seat; then throw his broken arm over the wood, until it reaches the armpit, and have a curve of wood in the middle, then hang on some heavy thing or the assistant stretches it down; then let the surgeon set the fracture evenly with his hands together, until the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one supports the patient on his back, and ties his hand to his neck, then instructs two assistants that one holds that which is above the fracture with his hands, and the other holds below with a linen cloth, and each stretches to his part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you want the traction to be stronger, then pull a linen cloth from below the fracture, and above the fracture, and let each of the assistants stretch to his part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is close to the head of the shoulder, then you must place a medium-sized linen cloth under the armpit, and another towards the side, below the fracture; and also if the fracture is towards the side, then you must place a linen cloth lightly, without effort, until the fracture is even on the place, and on the side; then set the fracture evenly, as it should be, and pull it, if no abscess forms there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess forms there, then do not pull it until seven days, and put on wool moistened in vinegar and rose oil, until the abscess is calmed; then pull it, and the manner of pulling is that you put the plaster on the fracture, then assemble the arm on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and put the cloth, and pull on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its proper place, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone might move, then use splints, and put on the fracture a splint larger and stronger than the others, and let there be two fingers' breadth between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture three fingers' breadth on each side; then pull on the splints, as I have said at the beginning of the chapter on the fracture, more strongly and less in separating.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the placement of the splints, and the binding, as we have said, at the time that you restore the broken limb, and you fear a hot abscess, then leave it bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then look every three days at the binding, so that no itching or swelling comes there, or that nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	Then correct it, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accident occurs, then do not unbind it except after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and have his hands on his stomach; and put under the shoulder a cushion full of wool evenly, and look every hour of the day or night, that the shape of the broken limb does not move, or that the bandages are not loosened; then correct it by the virtue of medicine, and give him the food that we have mentioned before, in such a way that the food is at first thin; and when he begins to recover, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be completely healed in forty days; and then one should unbind it and administer baths and ointments to heal the place.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is severe and swollen, it remains unbound for fifty days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	Of the fracture of the arm.
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "foscile," of which one is small, and that is the one which follows the little finger; and the other is large, and that is the one which is below, towards the little finger; by chance the large foscile breaks alone, or the small one, and by chance both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small foscile is broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing; and when the large one is broken, the healing is difficult, and more serious than when both are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small foscile which is broken alone, then it should be extended slightly, and set even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large foscile, then it should be pulled more strongly; and extend it on a cushion, and hold the little finger of the hand higher than the others, and the little fingers lower than the other fingers, and let the patient be crossed over himself, and a cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient suffers no pain; then let one attendant extend the arm at the lower part of his hand, or with a linen band, and another attendant at the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then let the physician set it even, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, then put each one in its place, and if there is any separated piece that pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut it and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in a separate chapter; then take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of the resetting, hot abscesses arise, then glue a cloth of cerote made of rose oil and white wax, which is neither too hard nor too soft; and bind the cloth on top subtly, until the hot abscesses are appeased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the cerote, and apply the plaster of the mill's powder with plenty of egg, then apply the splints, and let the splint over the fracture always be stronger, and a little wider than the others; and know that there should be six splints on the arm in various positions: whether the fracture is in one of the bones, or in two; and pull more above the fracture than elsewhere, and always less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths that are over the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the threads, with which it is bound, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And examine the limb and the binding after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some bad accident comes to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you must bathe the limb with warm water, until that itching is appeased; and do not let the limb rest tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then recommence the binding, and if the binding is loosened and the bones separated, and similar things, then redress it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And take care that nourishment can reach the limb, for if it is too tight, then you must loosen it a little, and leave it so for a few days, until nourishment flows to it, and then tighten it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said comes to the patient, then do not unbind it until twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	or around, then hang his hands on his neck, and let his shoulders be even, and guard against movement and fidgeting, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in thirty or thirty-five days, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and complexions of the humors.
de la brisure de la main	Of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and the knuckles of the fingers, few fractures occur, and often only sprains happen.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or sprained, the patient must sit cross-legged, and sit straight in front of him evenly; then place his hand on a stretched cloth, and let the attendant straighten the broken bones, and align them, until they are well-joined; and apply the plaster and lint, if no abscesses form, then apply a splint according to the size of the area; and let it be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is on the inside around the belly of the palm, make a sphere of cloths, and instruct the patient to hold it to his broken palm; and then bind it with a long cloth, and let the splint of soft leather be as large as the palm of the hand, and bind it as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the outside, you must place one splint on top, and another underneath in the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it all around the hand, and tighten the binding between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture occurs in any of the knuckles of the fingers, if it is the thumb, align it as necessary; and bind it with the palm, and if you wish, place a small straight splint to lift the fracture, and prevent movement; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as the index finger or one of the others, align it, and bind it with the healthy finger that is next to it; or you bind them all together, whichever is better, or you place a splint on it, as with the thumb; and take care in the restoration and in the treatment of a hot abscess, and treat what occurs there, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken thigh.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and one sees it well when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is that one binds one bandage above the fracture, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each attendant extends his bandage to his side equally; and this is when the fracture is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is close to the root of the thigh, let one of the bandages be towards the groin, and the other bandage below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And likewise if it is close to the knee, then let the bandage be near the knee, and let the extension be below; then let the surgeon set the bone even with his two hands, until it is according to its natural form, and then apply the plaster, and bind it, if no abscess forms there.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside, then return to your work and your treatment; the binding is done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap around the fracture one doubled hard bandage in two or three layers, and let the excess remain, then turn the leg until the heel comes to the root of the buttock, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg, near the knee below, and let the ends of the thread come up above; then turn the bandage over the leg and over the thigh, then place splints on the fracture, and place a splint on the leg bone; then fill the empty space between the leg and thigh with soft cloths to make the constriction even, then begin to bind firmly three or four turns over the fracture; and the higher you go above the fracture, the less you constrict; then take hold of the two ends of the thread that you have put between the leg and the thigh, and tie three splints which are above, then return below to the end of the thread, until you come near the foot; and constrict it, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, provided that neither abscess nor swelling nor anything similar appears.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, then unbind it, and treat what has appeared, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that protrude, it is necessary to remove them, if one can; and if one cannot, then it is necessary to open the place, and draw out pus; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken so that splints are applied, as in the shoulder and arm; however, in the restoration thus made, the patient does not limp.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in fifty days, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the kneecap
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the kneecap there is little breakage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a crack, or a hole, and occurs with a wound, and without a wound, and this one feels well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that one puts what is round to its sides, so that it is assembled as much as one can; then one applies the plaster, and puts a round splint, if you need it, and binds it as necessary, then observes all the instructions that we have said for other fractures, such as hot abscesses and other similar things; then apply to each accident what it requires, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the fracture of the leg.
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called by right name "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and the fracture is just as it is in the arm, and therefore the restoration is the same as that of the arm equally, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and one sees it well; and it turns underneath.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then administer extension, and set it even, and bind the splints evenly; however, if the fracture is bad, and there are several pieces, the extension must be less and lighter; and lighten it according to your strength.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two wooden splints that encompass the leg on one side and the other, and are the length of the leg from the knee down; then wrap around in two places one bandage above and below, and bind it in the middle also, and with this binding the leg cannot bend to the right or to the left, and so it is well; and some administer a splint the length of the leg, made of wood, and in it the leg is placed to prevent movement, and this is properly done in a fracture where there is a wound; and move the leg each day to see if there is a hot abscess or other accident; and treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fracture of the bones of the foot.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, fracture does not occur, but at the bones of the foot fracture sometimes occurs and at the toes also, and there is nothing but a crack in many ways.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if a fracture occurs in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping each other, then have the patient put his foot on the ground, as if he wanted to walk, and then immediately put your foot on his, there where the bones are raised, then press it until they return to their place; then put the plaster and lint on, and place under the sole of the foot a small board with two full ends, then bind it to the foot firmly, after you have wrapped cloths around, and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the binding, for you will find the bones even, whether fractured or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the toes broken, restore them as we have said of the fingers of the hand; then put on the broken toe a splint according to the length of the toe, and let it be a little wider, then put under the foot that board which I have mentioned, and bind it firmly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, then put on each toe a splint according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the board under the foot; and let it rest on the top of the board away from the sole of the foot, so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have said; and treat each accident as is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Of the fracture of the bone of the wrist.
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's vulva is broken, make her sit upright, then incline her towards her back, and let her be held from behind; then fill the vulva of the patient with cotton, and put in it as much as a fist; then bend the woman forward, and lift her back little by little, and then the cotton will come out until it reaches the entrance of the vulva, and the bone will return with the cotton; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back in, and do this for seven days or so: the fracture will be restored, and if you wish, take a sheep's bladder, and tie a tube to the opening, and put the whole bladder into the vulva; then blow forcefully into the tube, until the bladder is inflated inside: the vulva will return to its place and the fracture will be set; then it should be filled with cotton, and leave it like that for some days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the wrist bone of a man or a woman is broken, restore it as we have said for the hip bone; and these fractures are not hidden from one who applies his study and practice, and understands my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture signifies in many ways the right way of restoration: understand it therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's neck and put the penis inside it; then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for three days or so, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	Of fracture with wound.
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that it be healed quickly, so that the healings that we have mentioned testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, staunch it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then begin again to restore the fracture at that same time, or that day, if hot abscesses do not appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if hot abscesses appear, leave the restoration until the ninth day, until the abscesses are subsided, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause bad consequences.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on the uncovered flesh, it is necessary that you put it in place gently with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if extension is not sufficient for you to set it with your hands, then reset it with this iron instrument, which is seven or eight fingers long, and its width is according to the size of the wound; and for this reason it is necessary for the surgeon to have three or four, according to what he needs in each treatment of a fracture; and let it be round and somewhat thick, so that it does not bend with the compression on the limb in your work, and let it be sharp at the front, and thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called a "palainche," wherefore it is necessary that the curved head be placed on the head of the apparent bone; and push it at once, until it returns, and is even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot easily grasp the bone, it is necessary that you cut the head of the bone, until the instrument has power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone, as we have said, then cut it with an instrument suitable for this, either an incisor or a saw, to your ability; then remove what remains in the bone of roughness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	Then work until it is in place, then moisten a cloth in black styptic wine, and properly if it is in summer; and do not apply cerate or anything else containing oil to the wound, lest it cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer splints when you have reset the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the covering all around, according to the size of the wound, and take great care that the wound is not constricted with the fracture; and many times foolish surgeons have done this, and have caused the patient either death or sometimes corrosion; and let the binding be softer and gentler than for other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that bad consequences will arise, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then you must not apply splints; but wrap around, instead of splints, hard cloths, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days swelling forming at the wound, remove what you have put on with wine, and apply a wound-healing ointment, such as tetrapharmacum ointment and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must unbind the limb twice a day, morning and evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be positioned in such a way that the swelling runs down easily.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass, and it cannot heal but repeatedly swells, know that there are small pieces of bone, wherefore it is necessary that you probe the wound with a tent, and remove all those separated pieces that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula forms there, or another kind of corruption, then you must treat it, according to what is said in the preceding chapter.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken, and appears on the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and others similar of the large limbs, do not remove it, for many times death results, but leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall out by itself after twenty or thirty days, then heal the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of the swellings that come upon the fracture.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Many swellings come after the healing of the fracture, especially when it is near the joint, and the shape of the limb is unpleasant to see; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take heed then if the swelling is fresh: administer styptic medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocol, acacia, and similar others, so that you take some of these things, or all together, and mix them with styptic wine or with egg white or with vinegar; and put them on the swelling in lint, and bind it well, and do not unbind it for several days; and then unbind it, and begin another, until the swelling is removed; or you bind on a well-made piece of lead; for the property of lead is that it removes all swellings from the limbs; and if the swelling is already converted into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut it, and remove the apparent superfluity; or you scrape it with some razor, until it is removed, and treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed, and the limb remains weak and thin afterwards, it happens for many reasons: one is because it was bound too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and nourishment could not reach the limb; or because of excessive bleeding; or because of too much movement, not at the right time; or because he has little blood in his body, so he is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you make the patient eat, and make the body soft, until the blood is multiplied in him; and give him baths, and give him joy and merriment; then apply pitch to the limb, so that the pitch draws much nourishment to it, and bathe it often with warm water, until the nourishment flows to the limb; and it returns to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	Of the limb twisted after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bone is apparent, and the shape of the limb is unsightly, yet it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the fools who say that one should break the limb anew, and many foolish doctors have done this in our land; and this practice is condemned, and great harm comes from it, and perhaps death; however, if the knots and twists are fresh, they should be bathed in warm water, or softening herbs should be cooked, such as mallow leaves and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make a softening plaster, such as well-made diachylon, and take mallow mucilage, and mix it with hen grease or sesame oil, and make a plaster; or take dried figs, and crush them with flaxseed, and similar medicines that soften the hardness.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the knot is removed by continually and long rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let movement be given to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is old and hardened, like stone, and it needs to be removed with iron, then it must be cut to the bone, with a light, fine scalpel; and put care and diligence into the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation is the departure of a joint from its place, wherefore it cannot move, and the limb is misshapen, and the patient feels great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation occurs in someone, it must be immediately reduced without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the place swells, and perhaps one reduces it with difficulty; therefore, one must not move it when it is swollen: many times it causes spasm and other pains; however, when this happens, bleed the patient, then leave him until the swelling subsides; then bathe the limb with warm water and oil, then gently reduce it, and treat each limb as the treatment comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It rarely happens that both jaws are dislocated, and the dislocation of both is in two ways: either they are slightly dislocated from their place and somewhat softened; or they are completely dislocated, and hang towards the chest, and saliva flows from the mouth which he cannot hold, nor can he close his mouth, and his tongue is entangled with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is slight, it returns by itself in several ways.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and total, then you must reset it quickly, and not delay; and in such a way that the assistant holds the head of the patient, and places the tips of the fingers of one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on both sides; and the other two fingers should be outside, to maintain balance; and instruct the patient to soften his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the physician sets them evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if resetting it is difficult, especially if it is both jaws together, then bathe them with warm water and oil, until they are softened slightly; and do not delay in resetting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are reset evenly, and the patient's mouth closes well without being forced, then apply cloths soaked in a cerate made of rose oil and wax, then bind it lightly with soft bandages; and let the patient sleep on his back, and his head should be between two cushions, so that he does not move it neither to the right nor to the left, nor strain to chew, but eat light food, until the pains are gone, and the jaws are healed; and then eat what he wants lightly, and do not strain to open his mouth when eating and drinking, until the jaw is well healed and sound.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be reset at once, and are not returned to their place, then fever and usual swelling ensue, and perhaps diarrhea, and perhaps vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is fatal; and many times he who it happens to, dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	Of the clavicle.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The clavicle cannot be dislocated inwards towards the continuation of itself and the breast, and is sometimes dislocated outwards, and this is easily felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on his back, and extends his arms; and then press the place firmly with your palm, and it will return; then apply the plaster and bandage, and bind it; and the head which is towards the shoulder cannot be dislocated; except a little, and if it is dislocated sometimes, then reset it to its place, as we have said; then apply the plaster and bandage, and bind it, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed; and in the same way is the head of the shoulder reset, when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways: one is that it dislocates towards the armpit below; and the second is towards the breast; and it sometimes dislocates upwards, and this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate backwards by the shoulder, nor inwards by the nerves; and it often dislocates downwards towards the armpit, especially in those who have little flesh, for in those it leaps out readily; in those who have enough flesh, it leaps out with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And it sometimes happens to some men that there is a percussion or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and it is thought that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is necessary, then, that you examine it, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And the dislocation is known when it is down towards the armpit, and it shows a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a manifest difference between them; and you will find a hollow at the head of the shoulder, and below the armpit, feeling the head of the shoulder as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move it in any way; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you find it clearly by touch; and this type of dislocation is not difficult to reset, when it is recent, or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the attendant raises the patient's hand upwards, then places his elbows under the armpit, and forcibly raises the joint upwards into place; and the attendant raises the hand, and extends it upwards, then puts it underneath; so it will come readily.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said within a few days, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in warm water; and the attendant applies a softening and soothing ointment, such as a decoction of mallow, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and it should be applied; then let the patient be laid on his back, and place under the armpit an equal pad of wool, neither too soft nor too hard, then let the physician place his heel on the pad, and raise the head of the shoulder vigorously, and pull the patient's hand; and another attendant holds the patient's head so that it does not move downwards; that shoulder returns immediately, and if you wish, reset it in this manner: and that is that you have a man present who is larger than the patient; and he should be on the side, and put his shoulder under the patient's armpit, and raise the armpit upwards, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another attendant pulls the patient's hand downwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, let something heavy hang with him, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is reset also in another way: and that is that a long brand is stuck in the ground, whose head is as round as a pestle, and is neither too thick nor too thin; then it is placed under the patient, but with soft cloths on top, and the patient lies along the length of the staff; then his hand is pulled down hard on the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not wish to return for all these things that we have said, then do this treatment: take a brand of two spans long and four fingers wide, which has a round head to fit easily under the armpit, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie soft cloths on the head of the staff, so that the staff does not injure the patient, then place it under the patient's armpit; and extend his arm along the length of the staff, and tie the shoulder to the staff, and the arm to the head of the hand, then place the arm on a rung of a ladder of appropriate width, and let the hand be extended downwards, and let the body hang on the other side: the joint will go back in immediately.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in, in whatever way it may be, it is necessary that you put under the armpit an equal sphere of wool, then apply the prepared plaster of mill powder, with incense and egg white, over and around the whole shoulder, then bind it tightly under the armpit, and turn the bandage over the plaster, and embrace the hand to its neck, and let the hand remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he eat little, until the limb is strengthened, for it will heal faster; and then let him eat more after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place because of moisture that has come there, or for another reason, it is necessary that you apply cautery to three points, as it is described in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it loosens after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot raise his arm upwards, then know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder are cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation which is towards the breast and the nipples, or behind, is caused by impulsion and stretching of the hands, and another bandage is applied; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing, stiffness comes to the limb, and slowness in movement, let the patient use a bath many times, until that stiffness is lessened, and it returns to its former nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	Of the dislocation of the rib.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the rib is dislocated with difficulty, and returns with difficulty; and it is dislocated on all sides, and especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not hidden, for one sees it well and feels it well; and it is dislocated according to each form.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the diseased rib with the healthy one, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is broken, and he cannot bend his arm, nor touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it before hot abscesses come there, for if hot abscesses came there, it would be difficult to reset it; and perhaps it cannot be reset at all, especially when it is at the back; it is worse than other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and perhaps death comes from it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it is such that one can reset it, that you extend his hand with your two hands; and his arm should be extended, and the hands of the physician around the rib, above and below, and put the joint to its places together, or to the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and presses on the root of the palm the rib which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and it is that two assistants extend the arm, and two assistants hold it, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm on each side, after you have wrapped a long and wide double cloth; and when the physician has joined the joint to his hand, he should anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then forcefully put the joint in place until it returns; and when it is in place, he puts on a dry plaster with egg white, and binds it firmly, and hangs the arm around the neck of the patient, and leaves it for some days, then unbinds it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, unbind the bandage, and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, redo the plaster and the bandage, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then unbind it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, bathe and rub it gently, and press until it is relieved; or you put on the joint a poultice of fat mutton, then leave it one day and one night, then remove it, and have him enter the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint gently, then put the poultice back on, and then enter the bath; and do this two or three times, until he is healed; and if you wish, put on warm, moist cow dung with butter, and bind it on; thus it will return to its proper state.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand dislocates, and its return is easier than other joints. However, it must be returned to its place quickly, at the very moment it is dislocated, before the place is swollen, or a hot abscess forms there.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is that you place the affected hand on a table, and the assistant extends the hand, and you place it evenly, so that he places his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes until it returns. However, you must look to see if it is well in place; then the patient places the back of his hand on a table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, the patient places the back of his hand on the table, and the physician places his hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns immediately, it is well. If not, apply soothing plasters to the hot abscesses, and leave it thus without restarting.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it in place after some days, the joint remains crooked; and it does not harm the patient except that the hand is weakened, and cannot grasp anything at all: then know that the nerves or arteries are cut; there is no other remedy except cauterization near the case, and perhaps nothing else helps.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, apply the plaster we have mentioned, then bandage it and leave it for five days, then unbind it and leave it so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is some stiffness, moisten it with warm water, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on either side, sometimes on the back of the palm or on the belly; then extend the finger, and push the dislocation with your thumbs until it returns, then support the head of the finger, and bend it towards the part where it is disjointed; and leave it for two days, and then set it straight that day; and at night bind it, as we have said, and unbind it by day, and make it move, and bind it at night; and do this often, until it is straight, and do likewise if it is dislocated on the palm of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do likewise when it is dislocated elsewhere.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Of the dislocation of the spine of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine of the back or of the neck is dislocated, or if there are several dislocated, there is no cure, for death quickly takes the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the sign is that the excretions leap forth without will, and he cannot hold them, and many times some limb is softened, either the two thighs or the two arms or one. And many times the spine moves in four directions; that which moves in the rear is called "gibbosity": the cure is that you observe if the gibbosity came from infancy: if so, there is no cure or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from a fall or from percussion or from similar things, the ancients described methods of cure with great words, which are not always very profitable; but I have abridged it according to my intention, and have devised instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in gibbosity which comes to the breast in front, there is no device or remedy; and also that which comes straight on two sides, and one cannot cure except that which properly comes to the back, as I said; and it is that the patient should be extended on his face in a level place, and have straw beneath him, that he may not be injured; then fix a firebrand firmly in the ground at the head, and another at the feet, and tie a rope above the armpits of the patient, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two assistants hold the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two firebrands; and they should be well fastened, the firebrands as we have said, and the physician should place his palms on the spine firmly, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, then take a board three braccia long, and place it under the wall, and let the patient be lying on his side, and place the head of the board under the wall, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and let the physician place his feet on the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you wish, do it with a lathe which turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And it is that you fix two firebrands at the head of the patient a cubit apart, and towards the feet two others, and let there be between each firebrand, above and below, a palm's breadth of space in length; and let there be in each firebrand a hole, through which the lathe runs, and let the firebrands be firmly in the ground, so that they do not move; and between every two firebrands let there be a turning lathe, upon which the ropes turn, and let there be on two lathes two small firebrands a palm's length, to turn the lathe; and then tie the rope which is through the armpits to the lathe towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet to the other lathe, and each of the assistants turns his lathe with the rope, and the master sets the spine straight as we have said.
